## Base URL  The base URL you use in a REST API request is different for each customer. The base URL can be found by appending an API endpoint to your tenant URL.
Base URL example: https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/stories

PAGE 2: Setting up Authentication
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/0c1fb5e6ef1f46acb83771070084f124.html
Content length: 3747 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

## Configuring OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion Workflow (2-legged OAuth) The OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion workflow, is supported for server access to the REST API when your application is deployed on a SAP Business Technology Platform (SAP BTP) server and uses the SAP BTP SDK.
The SAP BTP provides an OAuth2SAMLBearerAssertion destination feature which takes care of the OAuth workflow for you.

### Prerequisites  - SAP Analytics Cloud tenant.

- An administrator account on an SAP Analytics Cloud tenant.

- A SAP BTP account for deploying the application used to access the API.

- Java application to access the API using the SAP BTP SDK.

- The SAP BTP account hosting the Java application must be configured to use the same IdP as the tenant.

- You must have a signing certificate for the local service provider for the SAP BTP account hosting the Java application.

### Tenant Configuration To establish a connection, you must configure the following information on your SAP Analytics Cloud tenant: - OAuth Client

- Trusted Identity Provider

For information on registering an OAuth client and Trusted Identity provider, see Managing OAuth Clients and Trusted Identity Providers.
The following OAuth client settings are required: - Name

- OAuth Client ID

- Authorization Grant

- Confidential

- Secret

If the SAP BTP account where your Java application is deployed is not configured to use the same IdP as the SAP Analytics Cloud tenant, see Configure Trust to the SAML Identity Provider Providers.
The signing certificate from the SAP BTP account where your Java application is deployed must be saved on the tenant as a Trusted Identity Provider. The signing certificate can be found in the SAP BTP account in the following location: SCP Cockpit  Security  Trust  Local Service Provider.
The Local Provider Settings should be set as follows: Configuration Type should be set to Custom, Principle Propagation must be set to Enabled, and Generate Key Pair if Required must be selected. For additional details, see Configure SAP Business Technology Platform as a Local Service Provider Providers. Copy the produced Signing Certificate and save it as a Trusted Identity provider on the tenant. For more information, see Managing OAuth Clients and Trusted Identity Providers.

### Application Configuration To configure your application you must: - Deploy your application to your SAP BTP account.

- Configure a destination with the Authentication Type OAuth2SAMLBearerAssertion in the SAP BTP account to connect your application to the API end point.

The OAuth2SAMLBearerAssertion destination will need to be configured to match the OAuth Client settings saved in the tenant. For details on how to configure the destination, see SAML Bearer Assertion Authentication. The following fields in the destination will need to be populated with tenant specific values: - Audience

- Client Key

- Token Service

- Token Service User

- Token Service Password

The Audience field should be set to the URL of the tenant being accessed. Token Service should be set to the Token URL that is listed on the SAP Analytics Cloud System  Administration  OAuth Clients page. The Client Key and Token Service User use the Client ID set in the OAuth Client saved on your SAP Analytics Cloud tenant. The Token Service Password is the Secret saved in the SAP Analytics Cloud tenant.
Once the tenant is configured and the destination in the SAP BTP account is configured, your application may attempt to complete the workflow. We recommend using the SAP BTP SDK to access the destination from within your application as it simplifies the OAuth workflow. For more information on how to use the SAP BTP SDK to access destinations, see these Tutorials.

# Get a Valid CSRF TokenYou must have a valid x-csrf-token before creating a POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request to the /stories, /scim, or /scim2 endpoints.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, including the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send requests to the service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header
| x-csrf-token:<token>
|




## Response The CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the POST, PUT, PATCH, or DELETE request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

## GET /v1/stories Returns a list of stories and story metadata accessible to the specified user.
Three object types may be returned: stories, models, and remote connections.
Only models based on remote data sources have remote connection information. All remote connections will have ID, connectionType and systemType attributes. Different remote connections can have different sets of attributes based on the connection type and the system type.

### URL Parameters  - HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- (Optional) x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- (Optional) x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true
Add this if you are using basic authentication against the token service. For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

- (Optional) include=models: The metadata of the models used in each story will be returned in the response.
For example, api/v1/stories?include=models.

### Successful Response   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 200
| Successful operation
An array of story, model, or remote connection objects will be returned.
Only models based on remote data sources have remote connection information. All remote connections will have an id, connectionType and systemType attributes. Different remote connections can have different sets of attributes based on the connection type and the system type.
|




- HTTP Headers:
- (Optional) x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true
Add this if you are using basic authentication against the token service. For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

| Returns

| Successful operation

## GET /v1/Resources  Returns a list of all stories and analytical applications available on the tenant.

### URL Parameters  - HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- (Optional) x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true
Add this if you are using basic authentication against the token service. For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

- (Optional) format=<Response_Format>: Set the response format to json or xml.

- (Optional) expand=<Attribute>: Expands on the specified attribute.

- (Optional) orderby=<Attribute> <Order>: Orders the results on the attribute passed in either ascending or descending order. <Order>can be set to asc (ascending) or desc (descending). By default, ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) top=<Number_of_Resources>: Get only the specified number of resources.

- (Optional) skip=<Number_of_Resources>: Skip the specified number of resources.

- (Optional) inlinecount=<Resources>: Specifies the number of resources returned. <Resources> can be set to allpages (all pages) or none (no count is returned).

- (Optional) select=<Field>: Get the specified field for a resource.

- (Optional) filter=<Filter>: Adds the specified filter to the request. Supported operators: and, or, not,eq, ne, startswith, endswith, gt, ge, lt, le.

For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/Resources?$format=json&$orderby=name desc.

### Successful Response   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 200
| Successful operation
A list of stories and analytical applications will be returned.
|




## Prerequisites   - You must have an SAP Analytics Cloud tenant URL.

- You must have an SAP Analytics Cloud user.

- You must configure OAuth to work with your application with the following settings:
- In Purpose, select API Access.

- In Access, select File Repository Read and File Repository Handling.

For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

## Error Responses and Troubleshooting    | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 400
| Bad request related to nonexistent property; please refer to documentation
There is a typo or mistake in your request. Check that the request syntax is correct.
|

| 403
| Not authorized to access the resource
There was an authentication issue with the request. This may occur if the user is authenticated by the IdP but does not have a corresponding user in the SAP Analytics Cloud tenant.
To resolve this issue, ensure that a user exists in SAP Analytics Cloud. For more information, see Create Users.
|

| 500
| A server error has occurred
The response body will be a JSON object with the following properties defined: status, code, and message. The information included with status, code, and message, may help you determine the cause of the server error.
|




PAGE 9: /filerepository/Resources
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/132338a059c741209c910770227afb82.html

## GET /api/v1/filerepository/Resources  Returns a list of all resources from the file repository that you have Read access to.
By default, the resources are returned in groups of 50. If you have Read access to more than 50 resources, the initial response returns the first 50 files and includes the @odata.nextLink property that provides the URL to the next group of 50 files.

# Additional Query OptionsThe File Repository Service API supports standard OData parameters.
The table below shows a list of the supported OData parameters that you can pass to the Resources endpoint to filter the results. For example, /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?$select=resourceId.
OData Parameters for the File Repository Service  | Parameter
| Type
| Description
| Example
|

| $select
| String
| Selects specific properties
| $select=resourceId, resourceType
|

| $filter
| String
| Apply conditions to a property using a valid comparison operator (eq, ne, gt, ge, lt, le, in)
| $filter=resourceType eq 'STORY'
|

| $expand
| String
| Retrieves more information on a resource's permissions, dependency objects, and ancestor nodes (breadcrumbs)
| $expand=resourceEffectivePermissions
$expand=ancestorFolders
$expand=dependencyObjects
|

| $count
| Boolean
| Returns the number of records in a collection
| $count=true
|

| $top
| Positive integer
| Returns top N values
| $top=15
|

| $skip
| Positive Integer
| Skips first N Values
| $skip=5
|

| $orderby
| String
| Orders by columns specified. Default order is ascending (asc), can be changed to descending. (desc)
| $orderby=modifiedTime desc
|




## ExampleReview the following table for some examples.   | To Return
| Use this Request
|

| A list of resources in descending order by their modified timestamp.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?$orderby=modifiedTime desc
|

| A list of resources in descending order by their modified timestamp. The total resource count is also included.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?$orderby=modifiedTime desc&$count=true
|

| A list of resources with a modified timestamp that is greater than 2024-07-31T12:29:52Z.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?$filter=modifiedTime gt 2024-07-31T12:29:52Z
|

| A list resources of type story that are in descending order by their modified timestamp.
This list does not include resource that are related to stories, such as applications, composites, templates, or insights.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?$filter=resourceType eq 'STORY' and resourceSubtype eq ''&$orderby=modifiedTime desc
|

| A list of resources that are saved in the Public folder, including all resources saved in subfolders, and that were modified after 2024-07-31T12:29:52Z.
This example query uses the applyManagePrivilege=true parameter. When it's run by a user who is assigned a role with Manage permission on Public Files and Private Files, the list of resources returned is based on the System view in the file repository.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?applyManagePrivilege=true&$expand=ancestorFolders&$filter=ancestorFolders/any(a:a/resourceId eq 'PUBLIC') and modifiedTime gt 2024-07-31T12:29:52Z
|

| A list of resources that depend on the resource with the ID 99D80085B81A2C6A5BB205C8A9FEC522.
This example query uses the applyManagePrivilege=true parameter. When it's run by a user who is assigned a role with Manage permission on Public Files and Private Files, the list of resources returned is based on the System view in the file repository.
| /api/v1/filerepository/Resources?applyManagePrivilege=true&$expand=dependencyObjects&$filter=dependencyObjects/any(d:d/dependencyResourceId eq '99D80085B81A2C6A5BB205C8A9FEC522')
|




## GET /v1/Repositories  Returns a list of stories, analytical applications and folder available on your SAP Analytics Cloud tenant.

### URL Parameters  - HTTP Headers:
- (Optional) x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true
Add this if you are using basic authentication against the token service. For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

- (Optional) format=<Response_Format>: Set the response format to json or xml.

- (Optional) expand=<Attribute>: Expands on the specified attribute.

- (Optional) orderby=<Attribute> <Order>: Orders the results on the attribute passed in either ascending or descending order. <Order>can be set to asc (ascending) or desc (descending). By default, ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) top=<Number_of_Resources>: Get only the specified number of resources.

- (Optional) skip=<Number_of_Resources>: Skip the specified number of resources.

- (Optional) inlinecount: Include the number of entities returned.

- (Optional) select=<Resource_ID>: Get the specified resource.

- (Optional) count: Return the total results count across all pages.

- (Optional) filter=<Filter>: Adds the specified filter to the request. Supported operators: And, Or, Not, Eq, Ne, Co, Sw, Ew.

For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/Repositories?$format=json&$orderby=name desc.
For more information on OData parameters, see OData Request System Query Options.

### Successful Response   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 200
| Successful operation
A list of stories, analytical applications and folders will be returned.
|




# widgetqueryThe widget query API lets you access widget data from optimized story experience, SAP Analytics Cloud.
You can use the API to get information of a widget.

## Prerequisites  - You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud tenant URL.

- You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud user.

- You must configure OAuth to work with your application. For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

## API Endpoints and Parameters    | Endpoint
| Description
|

| widgetquery/getWidgetData
| Gets widget data from optimized story experience by story ID and widget ID.
|




# widgetquery/getWidgetDataLets you get widget data from optimized story experience, SAP Analytics Cloud.

## API Request Details   | URL
| widgetquery/getWidgetData
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| URL Parameters
| Refer to the table below.
|




URL Parameters  | Name
| Mandatory/Optional
| Value
| Type
|

| storyId
| Mandatory
| ID of the story.
| string
|

| widgetId
| Mandatory
| ID of the widget, for example, Chart_1.
| string
|

| type
| Mandatory
| The supported value is kpiTile, which returns the format of SAP Mobile Start KPI monitoring tiles.
| string
|




## Sample Request 

```
https://<TENANT_URL>/widgetquery/getWidgetData?storyId=<STORY_ID>&widgetId=Chart_1&type=kpiTile
```




## Successful Sample Response
### Response Body 

```
{
"info": "QuarterEnds!",
"infoState": "Positive",
"number": 56985390.41,
"numberDigits": 1,
"numberState": "None",
"numberUnit": "EUR",
"stateArrow": "Up",
"subtitle": "in Million EUR",
"title": "Gross Margin"
}
```




### Possible Error Codes   | HTTP Status Code
| Error Code
| Description
|

| 400
| PARAM_NOT_VALID
| Story ID and widget ID are required.
|

| STORY_TYPE_NOT_SUPPORTED
| Only optimized stories are supported.
|

| WIDGET_TYPE_NOT_SUPPORTED
| Only charts are supported.
|

| 401
| UNAUTHORIZATION
| You need to have the read permission for the model.
|

| 404
| STORY_NOT_FOUND
| The story couldn’t be found by the given ID.
|

| WIDGET_NOT_FOUND
| The widget couldn’t be found by the given ID.
|

| 500
| UNEXPECTED
| There’re other errors than the listed ones.
|

| 503
| TARGET_SERVER_NOT_REACHABLE
| The server is currently unreachable.
|

PAGE 14: api/v1/dataexport
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/db62fd76514b48f8b71d695360320f4a.html
Content length: 877 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

## Data Export Service Cloud Data Integration The Data Export Service is a Cloud Data Integration (CDI) service, ensuring it can easily be integrated with any existing SAP solution which provides a CDI connector
As a CDI service, it provides an Administration service and a Providers service. The Administration service exposes a catalog of all available data providers, whereas the Providers service can expose both the data and metadata of each provider.
Simply put, the Administration service allows users to view and list SAP Analytics Cloud systems (Namespaces) as well as the models available on each system (Providers). The Providers service allows users to view and extract the underlying data for each provider.
A Namespace corresponds with an SAP Analytics Cloud system.
A Provider corresponds to a model or currency table available on an SAP Analytics Cloud system.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PAGE 15: Data Export API Changelog
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/644d83e8b56349b98d2f00ab1cf58fe9.html
Content length: 8646 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Data Export API ChangelogFind out what's new in the Data Export Service API.

## Version 1.4.0
### Fact Data Aggregation The Data Export API introduces a new FactDataAggregation entitySetName that allows user to export aggregated fact data, as well as track changes to this data through the delta functionality.
To export aggregated fact data, users need to specify which dimensions and measures they want to export using the $select property, and the remaining dimensions will be aggregated.
To track the changes to these aggregations, we use the same subscriptions concept that exists in the Data Export API, with two specific EntitySetName and Selection properties, like in the following POST request:

```
{
"NamespaceID": "sac",
"ProviderID": <Provider_ID>
"EntitySetName": FactDataAggregation",
"Selection": "DimensionA,DimensionB,MeasureC"
}
```




To create a subscription via GET Request, users will make a request to the {BaseURL}/providers/sac/<ProviderID>/FactDataAggregation?$select=DimensionA,DimensionB,MeasureC endpoint, using the 'Prefer': 'odata.track-changes': 

```
{
"NamespaceID": "sac",
"ProviderID": <Provider_ID>
"EntitySetName": FactDataAggregation",
"Selection": "DimensionA,DimensionB,MeasureC"
}
```




### Currency Properties The Data Export API specification available on Business Accelerator Hub has been updated to include rate properties (Currency Conversion tables) exposed in a 3-legged request: 

```
"@des.currency_table_version": "string",
"@des.user_privilege.read": "string",
"@des.user_privilege.create": "string",
"@des.user_privilege.update": "string",
"@des.rateID": "string"
```




## Version 1.3.2 The Data Export API now exposes the following additional properties: - Pagination
- nextentity

- nextentityorder

- contextid

- Custom Annotations
- NumberOfPropertiesPerEntity

- totalNumberOfCells

- uncompressedResponseSizeInBytes

## Version 1.3.1The Data Export API specification available on Business Accelerator Hub has now been updated. The following changes were introduced to the EDMX file: - Property tags have introduced a nullable attribute with the value set to false for the following properties:
- ProviderID

- NamespaceID

- SubscriptionID

- The EntitySet annotation tags have had a new attribute added named "Term". The term values are respective of the PropertyValue contained within. They are as follows:
- Term="Capabilities.InsertRestrictions" was added for "Insertable" property.

- Term="Capabilities.UpdateRestrictions" was added for "Updatable" property.

- Term="Capabilities.DeleteRestrictions" was added for "Deletable" property.

These changes were made to respect CAP project parsing of EDMX files.

## Version 1.3.0 The Data Export API now allows users to create subscriptions with an entitySetName of FactDataDifference, in which records within delta subscriptions contains the difference between the old and new measure values. These subscriptions can be created either by post request, or get request.
To create a FactDataDifference subscription via POST Request, specify the entitySetName as FactDataDifference in the body when sending the request to /administration/Subscriptions, like so:

```
{
"NamespaceID": "sac",
"ProviderID": <Provider_ID>
"EntitySetName": FactDataDifference"
}
```




This allows you to track changes to the model you specify in the ProviderID section.
To create a subscription via GET Request, make a request to {BaseURL}/providers/sac/<ProviderID>/FactDataDifference, with the following header:- Prefer: odata.track-changes

## Version 1.2.1 Added new query parameter delimiter which allows users to specify a custom delimiter when requesting a CSV response. As an example, a customer can query: /providers/sac/{ModelID}/FactData?$format=text/csv&delimiter=!
This will replace the standard CSV delimiter , with !.

## Version 1.2.0 The Data Export API now provides access to public dimension master data via the new sac_public_dimensions namespace.
By querying /administration/Namespaces, you will see the new namespace:

```
{
"@odata.context": "{BaseURL}/administration/$metadata#Namespaces",
"value": [
{
"NamespaceID": "sac",
"Description": "SAC Namespace"
},
{
"NamespaceID": "sac_currency_tables",
"Description": "SAC Currency Tables"
},
{
"NamespaceID": "sac_public_dimensions",
"Description": "SAC Public Dimensions"
},
{
"NamespaceID": "sac_unit_conversion",
"Description": "SAC Unit Conversion"
}
]
}
```




You can find the list of exposed Public Dimensions by querying the endpoint /administration/Namespaces(NamespaceID='sac_public_dimensions')/Providers.

```
{
"@odata.context": "{BaseURL}/administration/$metadata#Providers",
"value": [
{
"ProviderID": "T_C:GLaccount",
"ProviderName": "GLaccount",
"NamespaceID": "sac_public_dimensions",
"Description": "GLaccount - GLaccount",
"ServiceURL": "{BaseURL}/providers/sac_public_dimensions/T_C:GLaccount/"
},
{
"ProviderID": "t.TEST:Dimension_public",
"ProviderName": "Dimension_public",
"NamespaceID": "sac_public_dimensions",
"Description": "Dimension_public - Public Dimension",
"ServiceURL": "{BaseURL}/providers/sac_public_dimensions/t.TEST:Dimension_public/"
}
]
}
```




To get metadata such as column names and key columns for each public dimension, you can query the metadata endpoint: /providers/sac_public_dimensions/{ProviderID}/$metadata.

```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<edmx:Edmx Version="4.0" xmlns:edmx="http://docs.oasis-open.org/odata/ns/edmx">
<edmx:Reference Uri="{BaseURL}/odata/Org.OData.Core.V1.xml">
<edmx:Include Namespace="Org.OData.Core.V1" Alias="Core"></edmx:Include>
</edmx:Reference>
<edmx:Reference Uri="{BaseURL}/odata/Org.OData.Capabilities.V1.xml">
<edmx:Include Namespace="Org.OData.Capabilities.V1" Alias="Capabilities"></edmx:Include>
</edmx:Reference>
<edmx:Reference Uri="{BaseURL}/odata/com.sap.vocabularies.DataIntegration.v1.xml">
<edmx:Include Namespace="com.sap.vocabularies.DataIntegration.v1" Alias="Integration"></edmx:Include>
</edmx:Reference>
<edmx:DataServices>
<Schema xmlns="http://docs.oasis-open.org/odata/ns/edm" Namespace="com.sap.cloudDataIntegration" Alias="CloudDataIntegration">
<EntityType Name="PublicDimensionData">
<Key>
<PropertyRef Name="ID"/>
</Key>
<Property Name="ID" Type="Edm.String" MaxLength="256">

<String>NVARCHAR</String>
</Annotation>

<String>ID</String>
</Annotation>

<String>Member ID</String>
</Annotation>
</Property>
...
</EntityType>
<EntityContainer Name="t.TEST:Dimension_public">

<Annotation Term="Integration.SourceSystem">
<String>DataService</String>
</Annotation>
</EntityContainer>
...
</Schema>
</edmx:DataServices>
</edmx:Edmx>
```




The public dimension data is exposed through the PublicDimensionData entity set, and you can query the entitysets available for a particular provider (Public Dimension) with the following endpoint, known as the Service Document: /providers/sac_public_dimensions/{ProviderID}/.

```
{
"@odata.context": "{BaseURL}/providers/sac_public_dimensions/t.TEST%3ADimension_public/$metadata",
"value": [
{
"name": "PublicDimensionData",
"url": "PublicDimensionData"
}
]
}
```




The endpoint to query the data is /providers/sac_public_dimensions/{ProviderID}/PublicDimensionData.
This endpoint will by default return the full dataset, however similar to other Data Export modules, you can use standard Odata query parameters such as $filter, $select, $oderby, etc. 

```
{
"@odata.context": "{BaseURL}/providers/sac_public_dimensions/t.TEST%3ADimension_public/$metadata#PublicDimensionData",
"value": [
{
"ID": "#",
"Property_1": "",
"Property_2": "",
"Property_3": "1",
"Description": "Unassigned"
},
{
"ID": "Member_1",
"Property_1": "Value 1",
"Property_2": "Value 1",
"Property_3": "3",
"Description": "Member 1"
},
{
"ID": "Member_2",
"Property_1": "Value 1",
"Property_2": "Value 2",
"Property_3": "2",
"Description": "Member 2"
},
{
"ID": "Member_3",
"Property_1": "Value 2",
"Property_2": "Value 2",
"Property_3": "4",
"Description": "Member 3"
}
],
"@des.entitiesInPage": "4",
"@des.processingTimeInMilliseconds": "31075"
}
```

PAGE 16: Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Data Export Service
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/e4914540f5c04fd2b5b8be5675248be2.html
Content length: 2280 chars

# Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Data Export ServiceTo send requests to the service, you must first set up an OAuth client on the SAP Analytics Cloud system. This requires administrator access.

## Context
For any Two-Legged OAuth connection, the Data Export Service API runs a check on the OAuth Client used to authenticate. Only a valid OAuth Client can use the API.
An OAuth Client is considered valid for the Data Export Service API when:  - Purpose is set to API Access.

- The Data Export Service is listed under Access in the list of supported APIs.

To restrict an OAuth Client's usage exclusively to a Three-Legged flow, users have the option to define an alternate purpose or exclude the Data Export Service from the list of API access. Furthermore, note that while a valid OAuth Client designed for a Two-Legged flow can also function in a Three-Legged flow, the opposite is not true.

## Procedure
-  From the side navigation, choose  System   Administration.
-  Choose the App Integration tab.
-  Under Configure Clients, copy the Token URL. It will be needed later in this procedure.
-  Under Configured Clients, select Add a New OAuth Client.
-  In the dialog, add a Name for the OAuth client.
-  Under Purpose, select API Access.
-  Under Access, select Data Export Service.

-  Click Add. After you click Add, the application generates the OAuth Client ID and the Client Secret. Make sure to note them down, as these values will be used to send requests to the service.
After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: Access token URL, OAuth Client ID, and Client Secret.

## Next Steps
Using these three values, you can send a sample request in Postman.Let's configure Postman and send a request to the service.
First, let's configure the OAuth client. - Go to the Authorization tab.

- Under Type, select OAuth 2.0.

- Fill in the values as specified in the screenshot below.

There are two grant types supported:
- Client Credentials for Two-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards administrators.

- Authorization Code for Three-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards business users.

Once you have filled in these values, click Get New Access Token. This is the token you can use to send a request to the service.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PAGE 17: Get a Valid CSRF Token
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/500b6ce3aea34c5483dcd98c9048e4e3.html
Content length: 1029 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Get a Valid CSRF TokenBefore being able to create new subscriptions via POST requests or delete subscription chains, make sure you have a valid CSRF token first.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, or any GET request to the Data Export Service (e.g <tenant-url>/api/v1/dataexport/administration/Namespaces). The request must include the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send POST or DELETE requests to the Data Export Service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | CSRF Token Header
|

| URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token: fetch
|

| Auth Header
|

| Header Name
| x-sap-sac-custom-auth
|

| Header Value
| true
|




## Response The CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the POST request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

"@odata.context": "metadata#PublicDimensionData",
"value": [
{

"accType": "AST",
"rateType": "Closing",
"Description": "Total Assets",
"Language": "EN",
"scale": 2,
"numericShift": -3,
"unitType": "CUR",
"unitOfMeasure": "",
"formula": "IIF([PL030] = 0, NULL, [PL310] / [PL030])",
"aggregationType": "",
"exceptionAggregationType": "LAST"
}
]
}
```




## Note When extracting account dimensions, the numericShift property, which corresponds to Scale in SAP Analytics Cloud, is stored as a numeric value. The values are mapped as follows: - 0 is mapped to "None"

- 2 is mapped to "Percent"

- -3 is mapped to "Thousand"

- -6 is mapped to "Million"

- -9 is mapped to "Billion"

PAGE 35: /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactData
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/f7feb7c0792948e89cf89bcdb60db5d2.html
Content length: 1900 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactDataThis endpoint returns the fact data for the specified provider.
Using this fact data endpoint, you can also create a new subscription for that specific model, by including the OData header Prefer set to odata.track-changes. This lets the Data Export Service know that you want to track data changes on a given model.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactData
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| Prefer
|

| Value
| odata.track-changes
|




The reponse can also be generated in .CSV format using the $format=text/csv parameter in the request.

## Additional Parameters - $select: use this parameter to specify columns to select. For example, $select=MyColumn1,MyColumn2

- $filter: use this parameter to filter the result set according to the filter string. For example, MyColumn1 eq 'myColumn1'.

## Note You can also create a subscription using a POST request. This is useful if you want to specify an ExternalID by which to reference the subscription chain and a description to indicate the changes the subscription is tracking, or to filter or perform selections on the results. If you use $select, make sure to select all dimensions as they are mandatory. Only measures are optional. These fields can be specified in the JSON body of the post request, which should also include the NamespaceID, ProviderID, and the EntitySetName. For more information, see /administration/Subscriptions (POST).

## Sample Response 

```
{
"@odata.context": "$metadata#FactData",
"value": [
{
"Version": "actual",
"Account": "400000",
"Region": "USA",
"Product": "Mountain_Bike",
"Currency": "CAD",
"Time": "202201",
"MyMeasure1": 10.11
}
},

"@odata.deltaLink": "{BASE_URL}/providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/FactData?deltaid={deltaID}"

}
```



PAGE 37: /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactDataDifference
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/ced53741d1d4489d91fc9b64437c68bd.html
Content length: 1777 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactDataDifferenceThis endpoint returns the difference between old and new measure values for records over the time of the subscription.
This is calculated by taking the value of the measure at the start time of the subscription (old value), from the value of the measure at the time of subscription extraction (new value). For example, if your Cost measure was 100, and then updated to 250, the value of Cost in your subscription would be 150. (250 - 100).
This functionality is limited to Delta interactions, meaning to use this endpoint you must either: - Specify the header Prefer, set to odata.track-changes

- Extract data from a subscription (the request must have a deltaid query parameter)

If you are performing the extraction with the Prefer header set to odata.track-changes, this performs the initial load of the subscription. This means that all data from the SAP Analytics Cloud model will be exported, and this data will be normal FactData. The difference in records will only be returned once you begin to extract the second subscription, as these will be the changes that have occurred on the model. For more information on the subscription flow, see Subscriptions.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactDataDifference
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|

| Required Header (if no deltaid parameter set)
| Prefer: odata.track-changes
|




## Sample Response 

```
{
"@odata.context": "$metadata#FactDataDifference,
"value": [
{
"Account": "400000",
"Product": "Mountain_Bike",
"Time": "202201",
"MyMeasure1": 10.33
}
],
"@odata.deltaLink":  “{BaseURL}/providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/FactDataDifference?deltaid={DeltaID}",
}
```




PAGE 39: /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/AuditData
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/c56c2ede06e64e74bcab10ca1c4823a4.html

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/AuditDataThis endpoint returns the Audit Data for the specified provider when the Data Audit toggle is enabled for the selected model.
Audit Data stores all the data changes and timestamps in the Fact Data from the moment you enable the option. To enable the option, within the Modeler, click  to access the model preferences, and under Access and Privacy, click the Data Audit toggle. Once the option is enabled, changes can be retrieved using the Audit Data endpoint. If you disable the option, all Audit Data is removed, and you will not be able to retrieve the data changes anymore.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/AuditData
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|




PAGE 41: /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/{DimensionName}MasterWithHierarchy
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/f61659211b0040cd98bd81e61b1891e8.html

# /providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/{DimensionName}MasterWithHierarchyYou can check the list of dimension master data with parent-child hierarchy endpoints where relevant in the service document.
Each of these endpoints extracts parent-child hierarchy data out of one individual column of the mode. The entity set name follows this convention: column name followed by MasterWithHierarchy. For each parent-child hierarchy of the dimension, every row has three additional columns compared to the standard dimension master: - {HierarchyName}_PARENTID: the ID of the parent node in the hierarchy.

- {HierarchyName}_PREVID: the previous node which shares the same parent as this one in the hierarchy.

- {HierarchyName}_ORDERID: the index of this node in the list of nodes that share the parent node.

Account, generic and organization dimensions are supported.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{NamespaceID}/{ProviderID}/{DimensionName}MasterWithHierarchy
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|




## Sample Response 

```
{
"@odata.context": "$metadata#EmployeeMasterWithHierarchy ",
"value": [
{
"ID": "1",
"Name": "John",
"Description": "CEO",
"ManagerId_PARENTID": "",
"ManagerId_PREVID": "",
"ManagerId_ORDERID": "1"
}
]
}
```

# /providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/{limiter}___DistinctYou can limit the output of the currency table endpoint to select specific fields.
To achieve this, replace the "CurrencyTable" entity set name with "toCurr___Distinct". This will return only "toCurr" distinct column values.
You can add additional limits by separating them with "___" (three underscore characters). For example, "toCurr___fromCurr___Distinct" only returns "toCurr" and "fromCurr" distinct values.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/{limiter}___Distinct
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|




## Sample Request 

```

```

"toCurr": "USD"

# /providers/sac_unit_conversion/T006/ConversionRatesThis endpoint returns the data from the conversion rates data for the specified provider.
Material independent unit conversion is based on the standard unit conversion tables, and allow you to directly access all internal tables, rather than just getting a simplified view. Conversion still takes place between units of the same group, but you can now access the tables that store the groups, unit descriptions, and group descriptions, as well as the simplified view of unit conversion rates table.
This means you will be able to extract data for 4 tables: T006 (Conversion Rates), T006D (Unit Groups), T006A (Unit Descriptions), and T006D (Group Descriptions). These tables are exposed as providers, so you can see the full list of unit conversion tables with the below endpoint: 

```
{BaseURL}/administration/Namespaces(NamespaceID='sac_unit_conversion')/Providers
```




PAGE 48: Export Endpoint Responses to CSV
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/db13b8e75e7443a7a3332d177c9b3bdd.html
Content length: 2276 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Export Endpoint Responses to CSVYou can export responses to .CSV format for all endpoints that return an OData entity set.
You can do so by using the $format=text/csv query parameter. When that's the case, you can also request to have a custom delimiter using the optional delimiter query parameter. This allows you to specify the character or set of characters which separates column names and column values, for example: "delimiter=!".
The response format contains the first row as header values, and each row is separated by a new line character. Each column has an additional .CSV column at the end nextLink. This column isn’t filled on any row except the final row if a next link exists. When there's no next link, the final row is a normal data row that indicates the end of pagination.
This is used to avoid very large responses for server-side pagination. It is equivalent to @odata.nextLink with the default application/json response format.

## Request Example   | URL
| {BaseURL}/providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/FactData?$format=text/csv
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| text/csv
|




## CSV Sample Response File 

```
Version,Date,Account,SignedData,nextLink
public.Actual,201901,MARKETSHARE,402302018.3108333,
public.Actual,201902,MARKETSHARE,402302018.3108334,
public.Actual,201903,MARKETSHARE,402302018.3108334,
public.Actual,201904,MARKETSHARE,402302018.3108333,
public.Actual,201905,MARKETSHARE,402302018.3108333,
,,,, {BaseURL}/providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/FactData?$format=text/csv&nextEntity=...
```




In the example above, the three dots ... on the last line indicate that the line is longer than what is shown in the example.

## CSV Sample Response File with delimiter=! 

```
Version!Date!Account!SignedData!nextLink
“public.Actual!201901!MARKETSHARE!402302018.3108333!
“public.Actual!201902!MARKETSHARE"!402302018.3108334!
“public.Actual!201903!MARKETSHARE!402302018.3108334!
“public.Actual!201904!MARKETSHARE"!402302018.3108333!
“public.Actual!201905!MARKETSHARE!402302018.3108333!
!!!! {BaseURL}/providers/{namespaceID}/{providerID}/FactData?$format=text/csv&nextEntity=...
```




In the example above, the three dots ... on the last line indicate that the line is longer than what is shown in the example.

PAGE 49: Additional Query Options for Data Export
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/607f77a65c884c41a97d3f1e5a55109f.html
Content length: 4150 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Additional Query Options for Data ExportThe Data Export Service API supports standard OData parameters.
The tables below lists the additional supported parameters that you can use to filter out results when sending requests.
Additional Parameters for the Administration Service  | Parameter
| Type
| Description
| Example
|

| $select

| String
| Selects specific columns.
| $select=MyColumn1,MyColumn2
|

| $top
| Positive Integer
| Returns top N values.
| $top=15
|

| $skip
| Positive Integer
| Skips first N Values.
| $skip=5
|

| pagesize
| Positive Integer
| Returns N number of entities in the page.
| pagesize=5
|

| package
| Positive Integer
| Returns the Nth package.
| package=2
|

| $orderby
| String
| Orders by columns specified. Default order is ascending (asc), can be changed to descending. (desc)
| $orderby=MyMeasure1 desc
|

| $filter - all logical operators (eq, ne, gt, lt, ge, le)
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Applies logical OData filters.
| $filter=Region eq 'REG0001'
The Unassigned Value # value must be escaped using %23.
$filter=Region eq '%23'
|

| $filter - contains()
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column contains defined value.
| $filter=contains(Currency,'EUR')
|

| $filter - startswith()
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column starts with defined value.
| $filter=startswith(Account,'6')
|

| $filter - endswith()
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column ends with defined value.
| $filter=endswith(Region,'4')
|

| $filter - and
| Boolean
| OData logical “and”
| $filter=MyMeasure1 gt 0 and MyMeasure1 lt 10000
|

| $filter - or
| Boolean
| OData logical “or”
| $filter=MyMeasure1 gt 0 or MyMeasure1 lt 10000
|

| $filter - not
| Boolean
| OData logical “not”
| $filter=not contains(Currency,'EUR') and MyMeasure1 gt 0
|

| $filter - ()
| Boolean
| Parenthesis for filter operations.
|
$filter=(contains(Currency,'EUR') or contains(Currency,'USD')) and MyMeasure1 gt 0$filter=(Account eq '400000' or Account eq '400100') and Region eq 'REG0001'
$filter=(Currency eq 'EUR' or Currency eq 'CAD') and (Product eq 'PRD0004' or Product eq 'PRD0003')
|

| $count
| Boolean
| Returns the number of entities in the result set, with any filters (if specified). Will be annotated by @odata.count key.
| $count=true
|




Additional Parameters for the Provider Service  | Parameter
| Type
| Description
| Example
|

| $filter=(Account eq '400000' or Account eq '400100') and$filter - all logical operators (eq, ne, gt, lt, ge, le)
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Applies logical OData filters.
| $filter=Region eq 'REG0001'

| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column contains defined value.

| $filter - startswith()
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column starts with defined value.
| $filter=startswith(Account,'6')
|

| $filter - endswith()
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Returns rows where column ends with defined value.
| $filter=endswith(Region,'4')
|

| OData logical “and”
| $filter=MyMeasure1 gt 0 and MyMeasure1 lt 10000
|

|

| OData logical “not”
| $filter=not contains(Currency,'EUR') and MyMeasure1 gt 0

| $filter - ()
| Boolean
| Parenthesis for filter operations.
| $filter=(Account eq '400000' or Account eq '400100') and Region eq 'REG0001'
$filter=(contains(Currency,'EUR') or contains(Currency,'USD')) and MyMeasure1 gt 0
$filter=(Currency eq 'EUR' or Currency eq 'CAD') and (Product eq 'PRD0004' or Product eq 'PRD0003')
|

| $filter - tolower
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Changes the text to lowercase.
| $filter=tolower(Description) eq 'name'
|

| $filter - toupper
| Matches with type of column operated on.
| Changes the text to uppercase.
| $filter=toupper(NamespaceID) eq 'SAC'

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PAGE 50: Pagination of Exported Data
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/5b054ae15e1f415e8d4bdfc6dd5ff585.html
Content length: 465 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Pagination of Exported DataIn some cases, the full response cannot be returned in one page due to the page size query option or the response size limit enforced by the service.
In this case, a next link annotated by the @odata.nextLink is provided at the end of the response, which allows you to move to the next page. Send a request to the URL of the next link for the service to return the next page of data. No next link is displayed on the final page of data.

# Error Codes & TroubleshootingThis section explains error status codes and how to fix them.
| Error Code
| Error Message
| Action
|

| 1201
| API Provider cannot be identified or user / OAuth Client is not allowed to interact.
| The namespace ID couldn't be found. To resolve the issue, make sure the namespace ID is correct.
|

| 1203
| User or OAuth Client not allowed to interact with any API Provider.
| The feature toggle is disabled on every supported API Provider.
|

| 1204
| Provider not found.
| NamespaceID was identified correctly but ProviderID is incorrect.
|

| EntitySetNames list is empty.
| ProviderID cannot be exposed. Please verify API Provider system.
|

|

| 1212

| Check that the ProviderID and NamespaceID are valid. If the issues persists, contact your application owner.
|

| Enable the feature toggle.
|

| 1214
| Subscription cannot be retrieved.
| Check that the ProviderID, NamespaceID, and SubscriptionID are valid. If the issues persists, contact your application owner.
|

| 1215
| Subscription does not exist.
| Check that the ProviderID, NamespaceID, and SubscriptionID are valid.
|

| 1216
| Subscriptions for NamespaceID: <namespaceID> and ProviderID: <providerID> cannot be retrieved.
| Check that the ProviderID and NamespaceID are valid. If the issues persists, contact your application owner.
|

| The feature toggle is disabled.
|

| Amend the external ID to an non-existant one.

|

| Verify and adjust the request following the API Specifications.
|

|

|

|

|

|

|

|

| 1611

| Check that the delta feature toggle is enabled.
|

| 1618
| Max number of subscriptions allowed in the table has been reached: <totalSubscriptionsCap>
| Remove entries from subscriptions table.
|

| 1619
| Oldest subscription does not exist for deletion.
| Entity to be deleted cannot be deleted.
|

| 3405
| User does not have access to the SAP Datasphere space.
| You do not have the rights to access the SAP Datasphere space you have selected for the export. Contact your SAP Datasphere administrator.
|

|

| 3727

| New subscriptions cannot be created if the SAP Datasphere space in which the model is stored is locked. Unlock the space to create subscriptions on the model.
|

| Verify and adjust the request following the API Specifications.
|

PAGE 52: api/v1/dataimport
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/fe6efb8aba9444c6a3ce21eef02bba62.html

## Job Settings  You can pass job settings when you create a job to fine-tune how the job behaves and how you interact with it. If you don't pass any job settings, all settings are set to default values.

### ImportMethod Changing the importMethod setting allows you to fine-tune what happens when matching rows are found in the target model.

#### Update By default, the import method is set to Update. This method runs an upsert on the target model. If a row in the imported data matches the dimensions of a row in the target model, that row is updated. If there is no match, the source row is inserted as a new row.

#### Append Alternatively, you can set the import method to Append. In this case, the values of measures for matching rows are summed to the row in the target model. If there is no match the row is inserted as a new row. For more information about the Append method, see SAP Note 3420998 .

#### CleanAndReplace You can also set the import method to CleanAndReplace. This allows you to clean or delete subsets of your data before proceeding with the import. The deletion happens according to another job setting, called dimensionScope. This specifies the relevant dimensions, which determine what rows of data are deleted from the target model. The deletion happens according to what data in the target model matches rows in the source data. However, the important distinction in this case is that a match means that only values in the user defined dimensionScope must be the same. As an example, if the dimensionScope has a dimension exampleDimension, and you execute an import job containing a row where exampleDimension has a value of exampleValue, then any row in the target model where the dimensionexampleDimension has a value of exampleValue will be deleted. The dimensionScope by default includes the mandatory version dimension, but you can add dimensions by specifying them when you create a job. The dimensionScope is not relevant for the other import methods.
The dimension names specified in dimensionScope property need to match the dimension names in the target system. Custom names cannot be used in this setting.

#### DeleteAndUpsert & DropAndInsert Currency conversion tables support two additional methods: DeleteAndUpsert and DropAndInsert.
DeleteAndUpsert is the default import method for currency conversion. It allows you to delete the data specified in the DeletedData part of the request’s JSON body, and upsert data posted to data import service into the currency table. Like for Update, upsert here means if a row in the imported data matches the dimensions of a row in the target model, that row will be updated. If there is no match, the source row is inserted as a new row.
DropAndInsert allows for a drop of the current data in the currency table, and inserts all data posted to the data import service into the currency table.

### PivotOptions The PivotOptions job setting allows you to import pivoted CSV data.
When you create a job, you can also specify properties to define the structure of your pivoted data. Below is an example of the structure of a Pivoted CSV import, starting with the structure of the model.

```
Country | Generic Dimension
Product | Generic Dimension
Date    | Date Dimension
Costs   | Measure
Version | Version Dimension
```




Here is a structure example of pivoted CSV data you could import to a model. The date dimension is used as the pivotKey and the Costs measure as the pivotValue.

```
Country,Product,202301,202302,202303,202304
Ireland,Water,100,200,300,400
Ireland,Cola,500,600,700,-100
```




Before we can write this data, we must create a job first with the following mandatory job settings:

```
{
"JobSettings": {
"pivotOptions": {
"pivotColumnStart": 3,
"pivotKeyName": "Date",
"pivotValueName": "Costs"
}
}
}
```




- pivotColumnStart: This property defines the starting column index, in this case the third column is where the pivot key (Date) begins, any column after this index is expected to be a value of the pivot key “Date” which would be 202301, 202302…

- pivotKeyName: The name of the column, which is being pivoted, in this case it is the date dimension and we can see that all pivot columns are date values.

- pivotValueName: The pivotValue name is the column which corresponds to each pivotKey, in this case we selected the measure Costs. This means that for each pivoted column, the value will be the measure value associated with it. For example, if we take the row where Country is “Ireland” and Product is “Water”, then rest of the row is populated with the measure value for each corresponding date (202301 = 100, 202302 = 200).

If the pivotOptions are set correctly you may follow the standard import process (Step-by-Step or One-Click) to import your data to the target model. Each row is validated to ensure the length is consistent.

### ExecuteWithFailedRows The ExecuteWithFailedRows job setting specifies whether the job should go ahead when invalid rows are detected during the import. This setting is set to true by default, and you can edit it setting when creating a job. If set to false, and if invalid rows are detected, the write is canceled.
Here's a JSON example of a sample job creation: 

```
{
"JobSettings": {
"executeWithFailedRows": false
}
}
```




If the job detects failed rows in the /jobs/{jobID}/run endpoint returns the following: 

```
{
"error": {
"code": "xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx",
"message": "One or more failed rows detected. Write cancelled [2903]"
}
}
```




Details on which rows failed and why can be found using the /jobs/{jobID}/invalidRows endpoint. The job can still be forced to write regardless of the failed rows by initiating the /jobs/{jobID}/run endpoint with the overrideExecuteWithFailedRows flag set to true.
Here's an example of the /jobs/{jobID}/run endpoint's body with the override flag: 

```
{
"overrideExecuteWithFailedRows": true
}
```




### IgnoreAdditionalColumns The IgnoreAdditionalColumns job setting is used to set the behavior of the job if there are extra rows detected during the import. This setting is set to false by default, and you can edit this setting when creating a job. If set to true, any additional columns that could invalidate the data is ignored, and the data is uploaded without those columns.
Here's a JSON example of a sample job creation:


```
{
"JobSettings": {
"ignoreAdditionalColumns": true
}
}
```




### CustomDateFormat This job setting is used to convert the source data date columns format to a format different than that of the target model date dimensions. For example, you can convert “DDMMYYYY” to “MMYYYY”.
This job setting is only available when creating a job using the factData import method.
Here's a JSON example of a sample job creation with dateFormats:


```
{
"JobSettings": {
"dateFormats": {
"SourceDate1": "DD/MM/YYYY",
"SourceDate2": "DD/MM/YYYY"
}
}
}
```




### Reverse Sign By Account Type This job setting allows users to specify if they want to change the sign (+/-) of numeric data in the model from positive to negative or vice versa. This is available for account dimensions only, for members that have the account type of INC and LEQ.
This job setting is only available when creating a job with factData and masterFactData import methods.
Here's a JSON example of a sample job creation with reverseSignByAccountType:


```
{
"JobSettings": {
"reverseSignByAccountType": true
}
}
```




# Data Import API ChangelogFind out what's new in the Data Import Service API.

## Version 1.2.0 A new Unit Conversion service for Data Import Service now allows you to create and run import jobs to the standard unit conversion tables. This will allow you to inserrt, update, and delete custom units and unit descriptions in those tables.
You can see the new unit conversion tables which are exposed for import using the /unitConversions endpoint: 

```
{
"unitConversions": [
{
"unitConversionID": "T006",
"unitConversionName": "Conversion Rates",
"unitConversionDescription": "Conversion Rates - Conversion Rates",
"unitConversionURL": "{BaseURL}/unitConversions/T006"
},
{
"unitConversionID": "T006A",
"unitConversionName": "Unit Descriptions",
"unitConversionDescription": "Unit Descriptions - Unit Descriptions",
"unitConversionURL": "{BaseURL}/unitConversions/T006A"
}
]
}
```




For each table, you can find the required importType, metadataURL, and available job settings by using the /unitConversions/{unitConversionID} (GET) endpoint: 

```
{
"importTypeUrls": {
"conversionRates": "{BaseURL}/unitConversions/T006/conversionRates"
},
"metadataUrl": "{BaseURL}/unitConversions/T006/metadata",
"importTypes": [
{
"importType": "conversionRates",
"availableJobSettings": {
…
}
}
]
}
```




You can view the metadata for a particular unit conversion table, which tells you what the structure of the data should be when importing, using the /unitConversions/{unitConversionID}/metadata endpoint: 

```
{
"unitDescriptions": {
"keys": [
"SPRAS",
"MSEHI"
],
"columns": [
{
"columnName": "SPRAS",
"columnDataType": "string",
"maxLength": 2,
"isKey": true,
"propertyType": "PROPERTY",
"descriptionName": "SPRAS"
},
…
]
}
}
```




To import to any of the available unit tables, start by creating an import job for that table by sending a POST request to the /unitConversions/{unitConversionID}/{importType} endpoint, created using the table name and import type (retrieved from the response above): 

```
{
"jobID": "{jobid}",
"importType": "conversionRates",
"jobURL": "https://fpa139-01.orcastarkiller.canary.eu10.projectorca.cloud/api/v1/dataimport/jobs/{jobid}"
}
```




Using the JobID, you can send a POST request to the /jobs/{jobID} (POST) to post data to the job, for both upserts (Data) and deletes (DeletedData).

```
{
"Data": [
{
"MSEHI": "PLT",
"KZEX3": "X",
"KZEX6": "Y",
"ANDEC": 5,
"KZKEH": "Z",
"KZWOB": "W",
"KZ1EH": "1",
"KZ2EH": "2",
"DIMID": "CUSTOM",
"ZAEHL": 1,
"NENNR": 1,
"EXP10": 3,

}
],

}
]
}
```

PAGE 54: Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Data Import Service
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/dfd250c5cc584984aa00f93ee59d7fa8.html

# Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Data Import ServiceTo send requests to the service, you must first set up an OAuth client on the SAP Analytics Cloud system. This requires administrator access.
For any Two-Legged OAuth connection, the Data Import Service API runs a check on the OAuth Client used to authenticate. Only a valid OAuth Client can use the API.
An OAuth Client is considered valid for the Data Import Service API when:  - Purpose is set to API Access.

- The Data Import Service is listed under Access in the list of supported APIs.

To restrict an OAuth Client's usage exclusively to a Three-Legged flow, users have the option to define an alternate purpose or exclude the Data Import Service from the list of API access. Furthermore, note that while a valid OAuth Client designed for a Two-Legged flow can also function in a Three-Legged flow, the opposite is not true.
-  From the side navigation, choose  System   Administration.

-  Choose the App Integration tab.

-  Under Configure Clients, copy the Token URL. It will be needed later in this procedure.

-  Under Configured Clients, select Add a New OAuth Client.

-  In the dialog, add a Name for the OAuth client.

-  Under Purpose, select API Access.

-  Under Access, select Data Import Service.

-  Click Add.
After you click Add, the application generates the OAuth Client ID and the Client Secret. Make sure to note them down, as these values will be used to send requests to the service.
After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: Access token URL, OAuth Client ID, and Client Secret.

After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: - Access token URL

- OAuth Client ID

- (Client) Secret

## Next Steps Using these three values, you can send a sample request in Postman.Let's configure Postman and send a request to the service.
First, let's configure the OAuth client. - Go to the Authorization tab.

- Under Type, select OAuth 2.0.

- Fill in the values as specified in the screenshot below.

There are two grant types supported:
- Client Credentials for Two-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards administrators.

- Authorization Code for Three-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards business users.

Once you have filled in these values, click Get New Access Token. This is the token you can use to send a request to the service.

PAGE 55: Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST and DELETE Requests
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/9300c7aeea0645bfa34ad4f4f7aefd80.html
Content length: 1066 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST and DELETE RequestsBefore being able to send POST or DELETE HTTP requests to the service, make sure you have a valid CSRF token first.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, or any GET request to the Data Import Service (e.g <tenant-url>/api/v1/dataimport/models)), including both the x-csrf-token: fetch header and the x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send POST and DELETE requests to the service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| CRSF Token Header
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Header Value
| fetch
|

| Auth Header
|

| Header Name
| x-sap-sac-custom-auth
|

| Header Value
| true
|




## ResponseThe CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the post or delete request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

PAGE 57: /models/{modelID} (GET)
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/ed2baf9c39b54a2bb9f801c8add10e37.html

# /models/{modelID} (GET)Returns a list of supported import types for a given model, along with URLs to create import jobs for the import types supported, and a URL to retrieve the model metadata.
In the context of a business user, the reponse also contains the list of both public and private versions available for the import job.

PAGE 58: /models/{modelID} (POST)
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/e0690022f070454aaa9e1e8290b8372b.html

# /models/{modelID} (POST)Creates a new import job with a given import type specified automatically.
With this endpoint, you can also specify properties that change the behavior of the import job and how you can interact with it, namely the Mapping and JobSettings properties. These properties, when specified at job creation, are persisted, and exist for the lifetime of that job. However, Mapping can be overridden when posting data to the job. The importType, whether that is factData, masterData, masterFactData, or privateFactData is determined based on the Mapping property sent via the request.
JobSettings allows you to fine-tune how the data is combined with the target model based on matches of dimensions.
You can also set the content-type header to text/csv. However, you won't be able to specify the Mapping or JobSettings properties. With .CSV requests, the importType is inferred based on the column names in the header, or first line of the .CSV data.
After the job has been created, the endpoint returns the ID of the job with which you can interact further, as well as a jobURL, which you can use to post data to the job.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/models/{modelID}
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




## Sample Request 

```
https://your-sac-tenant-url.cloud/api/v1/dataimport/models/modelA
```




You can send multiple body formats via the request:  - Body with mapping property to rename two columns. In the example below, the import method is set to CleanAndReplace on dimensions Version and Bicycle:


```
{
"Mapping": {

"Bicycle": "Bike",
"Shop": "Store"
},

"JobSettings": {
"importMethod": "CleanAndReplace",
"dimensionScope": ["Version", "Bicycle"]

}

}
```




- No job settings specified. In the example below, the import method will be set to Update by default. Mapping specified to rename two columns:


```
{
"Mapping": {
"Bicycle": "Bike",
"Shop": "Store"
}
}
```




- No job settings specified. No mapping specified (empty body):


```
{
}
```




- In the example below, the import method set to Append:


```
{
"JobSettings": {
"importMethod": "Append"
}
}
```




- Content-type: text/csv


```
Version,Date,Bicycle,Shop,QuantitySold,TotalEarnings
```




## Sample Response 201: Created


```
{
"JobID": "{jobID}",
"JobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}"
}
```




## Error Responses   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 400
| Bad Request
|

| 403
| Unauthorized
|

| 404
| Not Found
|

| 500
| Unexpected Error
|




# /models/{modelID}/importType (POST)Creates an import job for a given planning model with the factData, masterData, masterFactData or privateFactData import type.
This endpoint also allows Mapping and JobSettings parameters.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/models/{modelID}/importType
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




## Additional Parameters - importType: mandatory parameter to specify the type of import job you want to create.
- factData: import data to the fact data table (Data Foundation).

- masterData: import data to all dimensions of the model.

- masterFactData: import data to all dimensions and to the fact data table.

- privateFactData: import data to the fact data table with a specified private version.

- Mapping: optional parameter that allows custom column names to reference internal column names on the model.

- JobSettings: optional parameter to fine-tune how the data is combined with the target model based on matches of dimensions.

## Sample Request You can send multiple body formats via the request:  - Body with mapping property to rename two columns. In the example below, the import method is set to CleanAndReplace on dimensions Version and Bicycle:


```
{
"Mapping": {
"Bicycle": "Bike",
"Shop": "Store"
},
"JobSettings": {
"importMethod": "CleanAndReplace",
"dimensionScope": ["Version", "Bicycle"]
}
}
```




- No job settings specified. In the example below, the import method will be set to Update by default. Mapping specified to rename two columns:


```
{
"Mapping": {
"Bicycle": "Bike",
"Shop": "Store"
}
}
```




- No job settings specified. No mapping specified (empty body):


```
{}
```




- In the example below, the import method set to Append:


```
{
"JobSettings": {
"importMethod": "Append"
}
}
```




- Content-type: text/csv


```
Version,Date,Bicycle,Shop,QuantitySold,TotalEarnings
```




## Sample Response 201: Created


```
{
"JobID": "{jobID}",
"JobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}"
}
```




## Error Responses   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 400
| Bad Request
|

| 403
| Unauthorized
|

| 404
| Not Found
|

| 500
| Unexpected Error
|




# /publicDimensions (GET)Returns a list of all public dimensions and their respective properties.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/publicDimensions
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|




- publicDimensionID: The ID of the dimension, how it appears in the URL of SAP Analtyics Cloud.

- publicDimensionName: The name of the dimension specified upon its creation.

- publicDimensionDescription: The description of the dimensions as specified upon its creation.

- publicDimensionURL: A URL which points to the next endpoint (/publicDimensions/dimensionID) which provides information about a given dimension.

PAGE 67: /currencyConversions/{currencyConversionID} (POST)
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/5b7149de4d594335865ad2fe4981f4d9.html

# /currencyConversions/{currencyConversionID} (POST)Creates a new import job with a given import type specified automatically.
You can specify the Mapping property, that is persisted, and exist for the lifetime of that job.
You can also set the content-type header to text/csv. However, when setting the content-type to text/csv, you won’t be able to specify Mapping.
If you want to import text/csv content with mappings, you can create the job in the standard .JSON format and post data to the job in text/csv. This job will then use the mappings passed during job creation for the csv data received.
You can select between two import methods: - DeleteAndUpsert: Allows for deletion of the current data in the currency table, and upsert of data posted to Data Import Service into the currency table. This is the method used by default.

- DropAndInsert: Allows for a drop of the current data in the currency table, and inserts all data posted to Data Import Service into the currency table.

After the job has been created, the endpoint returns the ID of the job with which you can interact further, as well as a jobURL, which you can use to post data to the job.
JobSettings is not supported in a currency conversion import.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/currencyConversions/{currencyConversionID}
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




## Sample Request

```
https://your-sac-tenant-url.cloud/api/v1/dataimport/currencyConversions/tableA
```




You can send multiple body formats within the request. - Body with Mapping property to rename two columns:


```
{ "Mapping": {
"validFrom": "validFromDate",
"rateVersion": "version"
}
}
```




- No mapping specified (empty body):


```
{}
```




- Body with an import method specified for the mapping:


```
{
"Mapping": {
"validFrom": "validFromDate"
},
"JobSettings": {
"importMethod": "DropAndInsert"
}
}
```




## Sample Response 201: Created 

```
{
"JobID": "{jobID}",
"JobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID} "
}
```




| Returns
|

| 400
| Bad Request
|

| 403
| Unauthorized
|

| 404
| Not Found
|

| 500
| Unexpected Error
|

# /unitConversions/{unitConversionID} (POST)Creates a new import job, automatically determining the import type based on the unit conversion ID.
This endpoint allows you to specify the Mapping property. It is persisted and exists for the lifetime of the job.
You can also specify a JobSettings property, which allows you to fine tune the behavior of the job. To get the available JobSettings for your desired unit conversion table, use the following endpoint: /unitConversions/{unitConversionID} (GET).
After the job has been created, the endpoint returns the ID of the job with which you can interact further, as well as a jobURL, which you can use to post data to the job.
For more info on posting data to the job see: /jobs/{jobID} (POST).

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/unitConversions/{unitConversionID} (POST)
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




## Sample Request 

```
https://your-sac-tenant-url.cloud/api/v1/dataimport/unitConversion/T006
```




There are several different body formats that can be sent in the request:
- Body with the Mapping property to rename the MSEHI column, add a default value for DIMID column, and set the executeWithFailedRows jobSetting:


```
{
"Mapping": {
"UnitID": "MSEHI"
},
"DefaultValues": {
"DIMID": "GROUP",
},
"JobSettings": {
" executeWithFailedRows": "false"
}
}
```




- No mapping specified (empty body):


```
{}
```




## Sample Response 201: Created 

```
{
"JobID": "{jobID}",
"JobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID} "
}
```

## Body  - Mapping: optional body property that allows custom column names to reference internal column names on the unit conversion table.

# /jobs/{jobID} (POST)Inserts data for an import job and returns rows that haven’t passed validation.
This endpoint also allows you to specify a mapping, as with the job creation. When that’s the case, the mapping takes precedence over any mapping saved on the job, and is used for the request.
It’s also possible to specify a default value for columns, which is inserted if nothing is specified in the supplied data. On top of this, the service automatically inserts a default value of “public.Actual” for Version if none is specified.
The data to import is specified in the Data property. Make sure the rows passed don’t have more columns than in the model, or they rows will be rejected. Primary keys (dimensions) are also mandatory, unless you have specified some default value.
The service also supports posting data via CSV. In this case, set the header Content-type to text/csv. An example for this type of request is shown below. If you want to have a delimiter other than the default ",", you can include the optional “delimiter” parameter in the URL, also described below.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




## Additional Parameters  - delimiter: optional parameter to specify a custom delimiter when the content-type header is set to text/csv.

## Sample Request  

```
https://your-sac-tenant-url.cloud/api/v1/dataimport/jobs/jobA
```






```
{
"Mapping":{
"Bicycle":"Bike"
},
"DefaultValues":{
"Shop":"SHP_01"
},
"Data":[
{
"Version":"public.Budget",
"Date":"202301",
"Bike":"TX100",
"Quantity":200
},
{
"Date":"202301",
"Bike":"AB100",
"Quantity":100
}
]
}
```




Text/csv post data request


```
Version,Date,Bicycle,Shop,QuantitySold,TotalEarnings
public.Actual,202303,TX100,SHP_01,100,1234.56
public.Actual,202304,TX101,SHP_02,200,10.00
```




Deleted data for currency conversion and unit conversion imports
Currency conversion related jobs offer an additional functionality that allows you to delete records from the target table before running the import. This functionality is not supported for import to models.
You can send records to delete from the target currency conversion table, following the same format as Data property in this body. Mapping and default values are supported and will follow the same rules as the Data section. Requests with only DeletedData section are not allowed. The Data section is always mandatory.
Regarding unit conversion, only the primary keys of the rows to be deleted need to be specified. Specifying any further column has no effects on the delete.


```
{
"DefaultValues":{
"toCurr":"EUR"
},
"Data":[
{
…,
"fromCurr":"GBP",
"rateValue":"0.86914",
"validFromDate": "20230101"
}
],
"DeletedData”: [
{
…,
"fromCurr":"CAD",
"rateValue":"1.45",
"validFromDate": "20221231"
}
]}
```




The body above will first delete the row CAD-EUR from the target table and then import GBP-EUR with exchange rate 0.86914 valid from the 1st January 2023.
Numeric Shift
When importing to public account dimensions, the numericShift property, which corresponds to Scale in SAP Analytics Cloud, is stored as a numeric value. You must use the numeric values when importing to this column. The values are mapped as follows: - 0 is mapped to ‘None’

- 2 is mapped to ‘Percent’

- -3 is mapped to ‘Thousand’

- -6 is mapped to ‘Million’

- -9 is mapped to 'Billion"

In the example below, the numericShift value is set to 'Thousand':

```
{
"ID":"ACC_100",
"accType":"AST",
"rateType":"Closing",
"Description":"Account_100",
"numericShift":"Thousand",
}
```




But should be set to '-3':

```
{
"ID":"ACC_100",
"accType":"AST",
"rateType":"Closing",
"Description":"Account_100",
"numericShift":-3,
}
```




Data Overwrite
When importing data to public dimensions, any column that is either omitted, missing or set to null will be deleted and overwritten.
| ID
| Description
| Location
| Product
|

| IT_100
| Item_100
| New York
| Coffee
|



```
