## Sample Response 201: Created
POST call with a valid row, and an invalid row:


```
{
"totalNumberRowsInCurrentRequest":2,
"upsertedNumberRows":1,
"failedNumberRows":1,
"failedRows":[
{
"row":{
"Version":"public.Actual",
"Date":"202301",
"Bike":"InvalidBikeName",
"Shop_Tienda":"SHP_01",
"Quantity":100,
"TotalEarnings":1234.56
},
"reason":"Row has more column(s) than expected, Row is missing values for primary key(s) - Bicycle"
}
],
"validateJobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/validate",
"runJobURL":"{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/run ",
"totalNumberRowsInJob":"1"
}
```




It is important to clarify that only valid rows are persisted in the temporary storage. All invalid rows aren't persisted. In this example, two rows were sent, but only one is now persisted.
POST call with two valid rows:

```
{
"totalNumberRowsInCurrentRequest":2,
"upsertedNumberRows":2,
"failedNumberRows":0,
"failedRows":[],
"validateJobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/validate",
"runJobURL":"{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/run ",
"totalNumberRowsInJob":"2"
}
```




POST call with 2 rows to delete and 1 to import:

```
{
"totalNumberDeletedRowsInCurrentRequest":2,
"failedDeletedDataNumberRows":0,
"failedDeletedDataRows":[],
"totalNumberRowsInCurrentRequest":1,
"upsertedNumberRows":1,
"failedNumberRows":0,
"failedRows":[],
"validateJobURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/validate",
"runJobURL":"{BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/run ",
"totalNumberRowsInJob":"1"
}
```




Both rows to be deleted are stored in the temporary storage. The single row to be imported is also stored in the temporary storage.

## Sample Request (T006 - conversionRates) The request below creates a new ABC unit, while deleting another XYZ unit. Note that ABC is a base unit of measure, for the DIM01 group. This means that a new group will be created in the T006D table (Unit Groups). For the import to succeed, the PRIMARY column must be set to "X", and ZAEHL (Numerator), and NENNR (Denominator) must both be set to "1". 

```
{
"Data": [
{
"MSEHI": "ABC",
"KZEX3": "X",
"KZEX6": "Y",
"ANDEC": 5,
"KZKEH": "Z",
"KZWOB": "W",
"KZ1EH": "1",
"KZ2EH": "2",
"DIMID": "DIM01",
"ZAEHL": 1,
"NENNR": 1,
"EXP10": 3,
"ADDKO": 12345.6789,
"EXPON": 2,
"DECAN": 8,
"ISOCODE": "ISO",
"PRIMARY": "X",
"TEMP_VALUE": 9876.54321,
"TEMP_UNIT": "C",
"FAMUNIT": "F",
"PRESS_VAL": 2112.34567,
"PRESS_UNIT": "BAR"
}
],
"DeletedData": [
{
"MSEHI": "XYZ"
}
]
}
```




# /jobs/{jobID}/validateValidates an import job and returns a list of rows as well as rows that failed validation according to model settings.
If the importMethod is set to CleanAndReplace, the /validate endpoint also returns an additional cleanAndReplaceAffectedRows property. This property displays a list of dimension value combinations that represent all rows that will be either cleaned or deleted from the target model before proceeding with the import. As a result, any row in the target model that matches the dimension values in the cleanAndReplaceAffectedRows property will be deleted automatically.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/validate
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|




```
"failedNumberRows": 0,
"invalidRowsURL": "{BaseUrl}/jobs/432661d8-8d62/invalidRows",
"jobStatusURL": "{BaseUrl}/jobs/432661d8-8d62/status"
}
```




The example below is a sample response using the CleanAndReplace import method.


```
{
"jobStatus": "READY_FOR_WRITE",

"jobStatusURL": "{BaseUrl}/jobs/432661d8-8d62/status"
“additionalInformation”: {
“cleanAndReplaceAffectedRows”: [
{
“Version”: “public.Actual”,
“Bicycle”: “TX100”
}
]
}
}
```

PAGE 79: /jobs/{jobID}/run

# /jobs/{jobID}/runRuns an import job and returns the job status.
For a long running job, the returned job status will always be PROCESSING. This means that the job is executed in background and the status can be fetched using the /status endpoint. For all other jobs, the final job status will either be COMPLETED or FAILED depending on the execution.
If the job status is FAILED, it means that there was one or multiple errors in persisting the data to the target model, currency conversion, unit conversion, or public dimensions. In the case of currency conversions, unit conversion and public dimensions, any row that is not persisted is automatically added to the errors table. You can check any row that isn't persisted using the /jobs/{jobID}/invalidRows endpoint.

## API Request Details   | URL
| {BaseURL}/jobs/{jobID}/run
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Content
| application/json
|

| Required Header
|

| Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Value
| <token>
|






```
{
"jobStatus": "PROCESSING",
"totalNumberRowsInJob": 1000,
"failedNumberRows": 0,
"invalidRowsURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/432661d8-8d62/invalidRows",
"jobStatusURL": "{BaseURL}/jobs/432661d8-8d62/status"
}
```

# Error Codes and TroubleshootingThis section explains error status codes and how to fix them.
| Error Code
| Error Message
| Action
|

| 1001
| Request job action is not supported.
| Execution flow is incorrect. Check current job state and call only the allowed functions.
|

| 1002
| Current user reached limit of maximum number of active jobs.
| Delete or run active jobs to allow creation of a new job.
|

| 1003
| Request not allowed on the selected job. Preconditions failed.
| Incorrect requested action. Please check job state and adjust request.
|

| 1004
| The following target fields are incorrect or do not exist on the model.
| Incorrect request body not aligned with metadata.
|

| 1005
| Unable to infer import type.
| API is not able to infer import type. Specify it in the URL.
|

| 1006
| Request body is incorrect or missing.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request body.
|

| 1007
| Current modelID reached limit or maximum number of active jobs.
| Delete or run active jobs to allow creation of a new job. For more information, see SAP Note 3491183 .
|

| 1008
| Unable to serialize mapping hash map.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request body.
|

| 1009
| A source or target column in the mapping is empty.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request body.
|

| 1010
| Request already in progress.
| Wait for the execution of the selected job.
|

| 1011
| Temporary storage does not contain valid records.
| No valid rows have been pushed. For more information, see SAP Note 3436537 .
|

| 1012
| User is not allowed to interact with selected job.
| Missing authorization.
|

| 1033
| Every row in temporary storage is invalid.
| Please use /invalidRows on the import job to see the reason. For more information, see SAP Note 3451247 .
|

| 1101
| Request not allowed on the system.
| Feature not active on the tenant. Wait SAC deployment or create incident.
|

| 1200
| The supplied content type is not supported by the Data Import Service.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request.
|

| 1201
| The request body sent is too large to be processed by the Data Import Service.
| Reduce request body.
|

| 1202
| Request body data incorrect or missing.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request body.
|

| 1203
| Request body mapping is incorrect.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request body.
|

| 1205
| Failed to insert data to temporary data store.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1301
| Invalid import type.
| Bad request. Review and adjust request.
|

| 1302
| Unable to create temporary data store.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1401
| Faild to validate table.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1402
| Failed to create table.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1603
| Job ID not found.
| Review JobID getting list of jobs to make sure that is valid.
|

| 1604
| Job cannot be retrieved.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1605
| Job cannot be persisted.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1606
| Jobs table migration failed.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1607
| Jobs cannot be retrieved.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1608
| Job cannot be deleted.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1701
| Model cannot be retrieved.
| Make sure that you have access to the model before accessing it. If you have it, create an incident.
|

| 1702
| Models cannot be retrieved.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1703
| Model metadata cannot be retrieved.
| Make sure that you have access to the model before accessing it. If you have it, create an incident.
|

| 1704
| Model does not exist.
| Adjust requested modelID.
|

| 1705
| Failed to execute select count table SQL.
| Create an incident.
|

| 1706
| Invalid URL parameter.
| Adjust request.
|

| 1802
| The model is restricted for import.
| Check whether the access and privacy settings on the model that allows for import using the Data Import API is enabled.

# api/v1/multiActionsThe multi action API allows you to have access to various capabilities offered by multi actions of SAP Analytics Cloud.
This API allows you to do the following: - Initiate multi actions.

- Query the execution status of multi actions after they're initiated.

## Prerequisites  - You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud tenant URL.

- You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud user.

- You must configure OAuth to work with your application. The Multi Action Service supports two OAuth authentication flows: - OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant - For information, see Configuring OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant Workflow in Setting up Authentication. As multi action APIs are supposed to be conducted under business user context, set Purpose to Interactive Usage when you configure the OAuth client.

- OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion - You need to have a trusted identity provider added to SAP Analytics Cloud. You can use the SAML Bearer Token issued by your identity provider to fetch the access token. For more information on how to add a trusted identity provider, see Add a Trusted Identity Provider in Set Up Third-Party Access with OAuth Clients.
The authorization code workflow generally requires the end-user to input the credentials to logon SAP Analytics Cloud explicitly to get the authorization code and continue the authentication. Since the consumption of multi action API can be embedded in a fully automated process with no user interference, the OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion workflow could be an alternative solution.

- You must get a valid CSRF token before making any POST request. For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token for the Multi Action API.

## API Endpoints and Parameters   | Endpoint
| Description
|

| /multiActions/<multiActionID>/executions
| Initiate a multi action.
|

| /multiActions/<multiActionID>/executions/<executionID>
| Query the execution status of an initiated multi action.
|




────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PAGE 86: Get a Valid CSRF Token for the Multi Action API
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/bbf348fa4cf64f82889ff0d9efb67cdb.html
Content length: 805 chars

# Get a Valid CSRF Token for the Multi Action APIYou must have a valid x-csrf-token before creating a POST request (used in the API to initiate a multi action).
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, including the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send POST requests in the same session. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token:<token>
|

| Header Value
| fetch
|




## Response The CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the POST request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# /multiActions/<multiActionID>/executionsAllows you to initiate a multi action.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token for the Multi Action API.

## POST /api/v1/multiActions/<multiActionID>/executions Initiates a multi action.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- Content-Type: <application/json>

- URL Parameters: <multiActionID> should be of format <packageId>:<objectId>. For example, t.TEST:CEEFOKMRUKJBY5BN47F1NS2L8G

- Request Body:
The following example request sets the parameter of different types.

```
{
"parameterValues": [
{
"parameterId": "TargetVersion",
"value": {
"memberIds": [
"public.Plan"
],
"hierarchyId": null,
},
},
{
"parameterId": "time",
"value": {
"memberIds": [
[
"(all)",
"2021",
"H1",
"20211",
"202101"
],
[
"(all)",
"2021",
"H1",
"20211",
"202102"
]
],
"hierarchyId": "YHQM",
},
},
{
"parameterId": "numberParameter",
"value": 42
}
]
}
```




If no parameters are required, keep an empty array in the body:

```
{

"parameterValues": [

]

}
```

# Messages and Error CodesThis topic introduces the format of a typical message in the response of the multi action API and its error codes.

## Message Format A message in the response of the multi action API is in the following format:

```
{

"messages": [

{

"code": "some error code",

"severity": "error",

"message": "some error meessage"

"details": []

}

]

}
```




## Error Codes An error code consists of 9 digital numbers in the format of "sccxxxyyy", and you can understand its semantics by referring to the conventions below: - s: severity

- cc: categoty

- xxx: task type

- yyy: message number

### Severity Definition   | Severity
| Description
|

| 1
| Info
|

| 3
| Warning
|

| 5
| Error
|




### Category Definition   | Category
| Description
|

| 01
| Validation errors related to parameter values assigned in the request body
|

| 02
| Validation errors related to specific step
|

| 03
| Validation errors related to multi action definition
|

| 80
| Errors returned from step execution. Multi actions public API is supposed to raise a generic error and contain the error logs returned from respective steps in details field.
|

| 97
| Other technical errors
|

| 98
| Authorization/object existence
|

| 99
| Request format
|




### Task Type Definition   | Task Type
| Description
|

| 000
| Not Related
|

| 001
| Data Action
|

| 002
| Data Import
|

| 003
| Smart Predict
|

| 004
| Version Management
|

| 005
| API Step
|



# api/v1/calendarThe calendar API allows you to interact with events in the SAP Analytics Cloud calendar.
You can use the APIs to perform the following actions: - Read information of a calendar event

- Copy a single calendar event or a complete hierarchy tree of calendar events

- Update the status of a calendar event

## Prerequisites  - You must have an SAP Analytics Cloud tenant URL.

- You must have an SAP Analytics Cloud user.

- You must configure OAuth to work with your application. The Calendar Service supports three OAuth authentication flows: - OAuth 2.0 Client Credentials (2-legged OAuth): This workflow allows administrators to fetch event information or start a planning workflow in machine-to-machine scenarios, for example.

- OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion (2-legged OAuth): This workflow allows administrators to fetch event information or start a planning workflow in machine-to-machine scenarios, for example.

- OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant (3-legged OAuth): This workflow allows business users to start a planning workflow or update the status of specific events.

For more information, see Setting up Authentication.

- You must get a valid CSRF token before making any POST or PATCH request. For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST and PATCH Requests.

- You can only access events in the SAP Analytics Cloud calendar for which you have allowed external API access.
As owner of a calendar event, you can turn off or on the setting Allow External API Access in the Create dialog or the Event Settings dialog. For more information, see Access Calendar Events Using the Calendar API.

## API Endpoints and Parameters    | Endpoint
| Description
|

| /events/{eventId} (GET)
| Fetches information of a calendar event from the SAP Analytics Cloud calendar, such as name, description, dates, and status
|

| /events/{eventId} (PATCH)
| You can use this API to update the status of an event in the SAP Analytics Cloud calendar. Events can be activated, suspended, or canceled, for example.
|

| /events (POST)
| Creates a copy of an event in the SAP Analytics Cloud calendar
|




────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PAGE 91: Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Calendar Service
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/14de88fde3944d7e952971686a1fbe19.html
Content length: 2373 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Calendar ServiceTo send requests to the service, you must first set up an OAuth client on the SAP Analytics Cloud system. This requires administrator access.
For any Two-Legged OAuth connection, the Calendar Service API runs a check on the OAuth Client used to authenticate. Only a valid OAuth Client can use the API.
An OAuth Client is considered valid for the Calendar Service API when:  - Purpose is set to API Access.

- The Calendar Service is listed under Access in the list of supported APIs.

To restrict an OAuth Client's usage exclusively to a Three-Legged flow, users have the option to define an alternate purpose or exclude the Calendar Service from the list of API access. Furthermore, note that while a valid OAuth Client designed for a Two-Legged flow can also function in a Three-Legged flow, the opposite is not true.
-  From the side navigation, choose  System   Administration.

-  Choose the App Integration tab.

-  Under Configure Clients, copy the Token URL. It will be needed later in this procedure.

-  Under Configured Clients, select Add a New OAuth Client.

-  In the dialog, add a Name for the OAuth client.

-  Under Purpose, select API Access.

-  Under Access, select Calendar Events.

-  Click Add.
After you click Add, the application generates the OAuth Client ID and the Client Secret. Make sure to note them down, as these values will be used to send requests to the service.
After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: Access token URL, OAuth Client ID, and Client Secret.

After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: - Access token URL

- OAuth Client ID

- (Client) Secret

## Next Steps Using these three values, you can send a sample request in Postman.Let's configure Postman and send a request to the service.
First, let's configure the OAuth client. - Go to the Authorization tab.

- Under Type, select OAuth 2.0.

- Fill in the values as specified in the screenshot below.  There are two grant types supported:
- Client Credentials for Two-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards administrators.

- Authorization Code for Three-Legged OAuth authentication, geared towards business users.

Once you have filled in these values, click Get New Access Token. This is the token you can use to send a request to the service.

# Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST and PATCH RequestsBefore being able to send POST or PATCH HTTP requests to the service, make sure you have a valid CSRF token first.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, including the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send PATCH request to the service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token:<token>
|

| Header Value
| fetch
|




## ResponseThe CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the post/patch request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

# /events (POST)Allows you to copy a calendar event.
As a result, the event will have the current date as start date. All users and files of the event are copied, as well as all child events.

## API Request Details    | URL
| POST/api/v1/calendar/events
|

| Request Type
| POST
|




## Sample Request  

```
https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/calendar/events
```




## Request Body
### Request Body Parameters   | Parameter
| Description
|

| referenceEventId
| ID of the event to be copied
|

| autoActivate
| Specifies whether the new event should be activated directly if possible. All users defined in the event and its hierarchy will see the event in their calendar.
|

| notify
| Specifies whether the SAP Analytics Cloud system should notify affected users about the activation of the event. This parameter is only relevant if you have set autoActivate to true.
|




### Sample Request Body  

```
{
“referenceEventId”: “exampleEventId”,
“autoActivate”: true,
“notify”: false
}
```




## Successful Sample Response    | HTTP Status Code
| Response Body
|

| 201
| 

```
{
“event”: {
“id”: “idOfEventCopy”,
“utcStartDate”: <UTCTimestamp in ISO 8601 format>,
“utcEndDate”: <UTCTimestamp in ISO 8601 format>
},
“links”: [{
“rel”: "event"
“href”: "/api/v1/events/<eventID>"
}]
}
```

PAGE 96: api/v1/content
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/eeace13cc37b4eed96064a7c5d8ee493.html

## Prerequisites You have to pass X-CSRF token, x-sap-sac-custom-auth=true parameter, and the access token to authorize your client application while sending any request to the API.
Follow these steps:
- Create a new OAuth client. Follow the steps in the topic Managing OAuth Clients to create a new OAuth client.

- Authorize the OAuth client. Follow the steps in the section Authorization for API access OAuth Clients of the topic Managing OAuth Clients to authorize the OAuth client.

- Add the X-CSRF token.
- Issue a GET request to the API endpoint. Example endpoint: https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/csrf
You must include the following headers with your GET request: - Authorization: Bearer <Access_Token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: fetch

- Retrieve the value of the HTTP response header named x-csrf-token.

- In an HTTP request that you make to the API, add the following:
- Authorization: Bearer <Access_Token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: <x-csrf_Token_Value>

Alternatively, you can also follow the steps for Configuring OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant Workflow in Setting up Authentication. You would then require x-csrf token if you're sending POST, PATCH, UPDATE, and DELETE requests. You can follow step 3 mentioned above and eliminate the x-sap-sac-custom-auth parameter to generate an x-csrf-token for authorization code grant workflow.
If you choose OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant, then you have to pass the following parameters in your request: - Authorization: Bearer <Access_Token>

- x-csrf-token: <x-csrf_Token_Value>

## Create an Export Job This topic provides information that is required to create an export job of private packages in the Content Network through an API.

### Context Once you have the API request details, you have to provide the HTTP body and the service parameters for the request. You can check the sample HTTP body and service parameter structure below and replace the placeholders with actual values.

Attributes in Export Job Request Payload  | Attribute
| Type
| Mandatory/Optional
| Description
|

| type
| String
| Mandatory
| Specifies the type of the job. The value should be EXPORT for creating an export job.
|

| serviceParameters
| String
| Mandatory
|
- fields (Mandatory) - contains the name, summary, and description of the export (package). It's an array of fields. Each field specifies different field (for example, name, summary, and description) of the package and it consists of the following: It is a JSON structure that supports only string values and defines the details of the export that includes:
- fieldTypeIt is a JSON structure that supports only string values (Mandatory) - Specifies the type of the field. It can be name, description, or summary.

- fieldI18n (Mandatory) - Specifies the localized value of the field. It's an array of object where each object consists of the following:
- langCode (Mandatory) - The language for the value of the field.

- value (Mandatory) - The value of the field.

- isPrivate (Mandatory) - specifies whether the export job is for private content sharing. It should be true as only private Content sharing is supported for this endpoint.

- privateItemsData (Mandatory) - specifies the following details:
- itemId (Optional) - specifies the item ID for the existing item when updating it with the modified content/metadata.

- parentItemId (Mandatory) - specifies the id of the parent folder under which the content is being exported to.

- permissions (Mandatory) - Specifies the details of who is the recipient of this exported content. Its an array and each object inside it specifies the each sharing entity (permission). If the content need not be shared with anyone or you are using Content Network file to share the content, then you can keep it as empty ([ ]).
- permission - Specifies a sharing entity and the content can be shared with some tenant by different means.

For sharing the content with a specific tenant use the below attributes: - tenantUrl - The tenant url of the tenant the content is being shared.

- landscapeId - The landscapeId of the tenant the content is being shared.

For sharing the content with a group of tenants having same OEM ID (partner) use the below attributes: - oemId - The OEM ID of the tenants.

For sharing the content with a group of tenants having same erpNumber (customer number) use the below attribute:  - erpNumber -The ERP number of the tenants.

From the above, (tenantUrl&landscapeID/oemId/erpNumber) any one should be present in a sharing entity (permission). The below attributes in permission specifies the access rights that are given for the sharing tenant(s):  - list (mandatory) - true/false - The tenant should be able to only view the package (export unit)

- read (mandatory) - true/false - The tenant should be able to view and import the package (export unit)

- write (mandatory) - true/false - The tenant should be able to view, import, export, and edit the package (export unit)

- delete (mandatory) - true/false - The tenant should be able to delete the package (export unit).

- overwritePermissions - true/false - specifies whether the existing permissions require overwriting during the edit export API request.

-  taggingData (optional): Specifies the tags that can be applied for the package.
taggingData value should be a parameter tag which specifies the tag details. The value of a parameter tag is an array of tag object.
Each tag object has parameter tagId to specify the tag IDs. You can check the supported tags with their IDs in Predefined Content Network Package Tags.

|

| packageVersion
| String
| Optional
| packageVersion is an optional parameter in the export payload. If not provided, the package is exported with the default version 1.0.0.
|

| originLandscape
| String
| Conditional
| Export inside My Content - originLandscapeId (optional)
Export inside Cross landscape shared folder - originLandscapeId (mandatory), provide source tenant landscape ID.
|

| objects
| Object [ ]
| Mandatory
| Specifies the array of objects to be exported.
Each object has the following attributes:  - xsParameters: It is required for export job. You should pass no value and leave it empty `{}` .

- serviceParameters: It includes the parameter includeData which specifies whether the data to be included during export or not. Pass it as below - "{\"includeData\":true}"

- objectId: Specifies the objectId of the object to be exported.

- objectName: Specifies the name of the object

- objectType: Specifies the type of the object.

- description: Specifies the description of the object.

|




### Response When the POST method to create an export job is successful, then the system returns the job ID as the response.

## Getting All Items You can get the public items in your Content Network through an API.

### API Request Details You would need the following information to get the items.  | URL
| /api/v1/content/public/<parentItemID>
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Content Type
| application/json
|

| Query Parameters
| Refer to the table below.
|




Query Parameters  | Name
| Description
| Type
| Default Value
| Example
|

| Permissions
| List the items that the user has specific permissions for
| String
The supported values are list, read, write, delete. Multiple values can be sent using the & operator.
| list
|  - Getting items on which the tenant has list permission: /api/v1/content/public/1?permissions=list

- Getting items on which the tenant has read and write permission:/api/v1/content/public/1?permissions=read&permissions=write

|

| itemType
| Specify the type of items needs to be fetched
| String.
The supported values are: - PACKAGE

- SUB-CATEGORY

- ALL

| ALL
| Getting only the Folders:/api/v1/content/public/1?itemType=SUB-CATEGORY
|

| tags
| Specifies the tag IDs to filter the items
| String
Multiple values can be sent using "&" operator.
| []
| Getting the items that has the specified tag ID (s):
<apiHost>/api/v1/content/public/1?tags=<tag_ID_1>&tags=<tag_ID_2>
You can check the supported tags with their IDs in Predefined Content Network Package Tags.
|




PAGE 111: Managing Users and Teams
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/ee11077e8a344ce99dfb77033eace581.html

# Managing Users and TeamsThere are several API endpoints available for managing users and teams.

## api/v1/scim The SCIM endpoint is based on the SCIM 2.0 specifications, but with some limitations. The SCIM endpoint provides fast retrieval of bulk information from SAP Analytics Cloud.
The SCIM endpoint uses a user id to retrieve user information.

## api/v1/scim2 The SCIM2 endpoint is a SCIM 2.0 compliant endpoint that includes additional functionality not included in the SCIM endpoint. For example, you can search for teams, and get information on your identity provider (IDP), available schemas, and resource types.
The SCIM2 endpoint uses a UUID to retrieve user information for data protection. An optional external ID parameter can also be added if the ID for logging on to your IDP is different from the ID used in SAP Analytics Cloud.
SCIM2 is only available for tenants running on a Cloud Foundry platform. If you have a Cloud Foundry platform, you can use both the SCIM and SCIM2 endpoints simultaneously.

## api/v1/scim3 The SCIM3 endpoint is a SCIM2.0 compliant endpoint that allows you to programmatically manage roles and teams. SCIM3 includes additional functionality not included in the SCIM and SCIM2 endpoints such as the ability to manage roles using the /Groups endpoint.

## CSRF Token When using either API endpoint, you must include a valid CSRF token with any POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request. For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

Related Information
Setting up Authentication
api/v1/scim
api/v1/scim2

PAGE 113: /scim/Users
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/da3dc52a0fd44da4b727c89d26326af6.html

# /scim/UsersAllows you to create a user or get a list of users.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## GET /api/v1/scim/Users Gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Optional: x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- URL Parameters:
- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request.
Supported Attributes: - username

- email

Supported Operators: - And

- Or

- Not

- Eq

- Ne

- Co

- Sw

- Ew

- Request Body: None

Example GET request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim/Users?filter=username eq "abcUser"
| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 403: Not authorized

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| 

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:ListResponse"],
"totalResults": 123,
"itemsPerPage": 10,
"startIndex": 1,
"Resources": [{<User Schema>}, ...]
}
```




|




## POST /api/v1/scim/Users Creates a user based on the information provided.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: User Schema
The following example schema creates a new user:

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:core:2.0:User",
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:enterprise:2.0:User",
]
"userName":"<user@email.com>",
"name":
{
"givenName":"<User_Given_Name>",
"familyName":"<User_Family_Name>"
},
"displayName":"<User_Display_Name>",
"emails":[
{
"value":"<user@email.com>",
"type":"work",
"primary":true
}
],
"roles":[],
"groups":[],
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:enterprise:2.0:User": {
"manager": {
"managerId": ""
}
}
}
```




For information on role assignment, see Assigning Roles to Users and Groups. For information on additional parameter options, see Optional User Parameters.

| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 409: User name conflict

- 403: Not authorized

- 400: User operation not completed: The maximum number of licenses have been reached. Please check your current license usage limits, then deactivate users, delete inactive users, or consider an upgrade to your plan.

- 201: Created

Format: application/scim+json (User Schema)
| The response should include the user information you provided.


```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:core:2.0:User",
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:enterprise:2.0:User",
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:user-custom-parameters:1.0"
],
"userName": "test.user@email.com",
"id": "TESTUSER",
"preferredLanguage": "en",
"meta": {
"created": "2017-09-06T21:22:26.258Z",
"location": "/api/v1/scim/Users/TESTUSER",
"resourceType": "User"
},
"name": {
"givenName": "Test",
"familyName": "User"
},
"displayName": "Test User",
"active": true,
"emails": [
{
"value": "test.user@email.com",
"type": "work",
"primary": true
}
],
"photos": [
{
"value": "https://myphotos.com/profile.png",
"type": "photo"
}
],
"roles": [
"PROFILE:sap.epm:Admin"
],
"groups": [],
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:user-custom-parameters:1.0": {
"dataAccessLanguage": "en",
"dateFormatting": "MMM d, yyyy",
"timeFormatting": "H:mm:ss",
"numberFormatting": "1,234.56",
"cleanUpNotificationsNumberOfDays": 0,
"systemNotificationsEmailOptIn": true,
"marketingEmailOptIn": false
},
"urn:scim:schemas:extension:enterprise:1.0": {
"manager": {
"managerId": ""
}
```

| See GET for an example response. The response should include updated user information.

## DELETE /api/v1/scim/Users/<ID> Deletes the user specified by <ID>.
When the user is deleted, the ownership of the user's files are transferred to the System Owner. The deleted user's public files will remain in the Public folder. Any private files will be moved to the System Owner's private folder.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters: id: <ID>

- Request Body: None

| Response
|

|   - 404: Not found

- 403: Not authorized

- 204: OK

|

# /scim/Users/.searchSearch for and get a list of users.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## POST /api/v1/scim/Users/.search Searches for and gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: User Schema
The following example schema searches for a list of users based on a username string:

```
{
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:SearchRequest"],
"filter":
"username sw \"smith\"",
"startIndex": 1,
"count": 10
}
```




The following filter options are supported in the request body: - (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request.
Supported Filter Attributes: - username

- email

Supported Operators: - And

- Or

- Not

- Eq

- Ne

- Co

- Sw

- Ew

Example POST request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim2/Users/.search
| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 403: Not authorized

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| 

```
{
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:ListResponse"],
"totalResults":100,
"itemsPerPage":10,
"startIndex":1,
"Resources":[
{
"id":"2720c223-7g76-419371904643",
"userName":"smithj",
"displayName":"Smith, James"
......
},
...
]
}
```




|




Related Information
Optional User Parameters
Assigning Roles to Users and Groups

PAGE 119: /scim2/Bulk
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/8ba90d3fc5b24d2fb181c716abd5c8bb.html

# /scim2/BulkAllows you to use to add, update, patch and remove users in bulk.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST operation.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## POST /api/v1/scim2/Bulk Updates users in bulk. Supported operations are POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: Method (POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE) and Path (/Users/<ID> or /Groups/<ID>)
The following example deletes two users:

```
{
"failOnErrors":1,
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:BulkRequest"],
"Operations": [
{
"method": "DELETE",
"path": "/Users/ce813e33-6130-4e13-90ea-1f3d3ed1d1f6"
},
{
"method": "DELETE",
"path": "/Users/6f0c4a7f-88eb-478f-9a2d-332ed7c56224"
}
]
}
```




Example response from deleting two users:

| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 403: Forbidden

# /scim2/UsersAllows you to create a user or get a list of users.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## GET /api/v1/scim2/Users Gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Optional: x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- URL Parameters:
- (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, username.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the user schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

Example GET request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim2/Users?filter=emails.value co "a"&sortOrder=descending&startIndex=3&count=2&sortBy=emails.value

- Request Body: None

| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 403: Forbidden

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| 

## POST /api/v1/scim2/Users Creates a user based on the information provided.

```
{

"name": {
"familyName": "test",
"givenName": "test",
"formatted": "test"
},

"preferredLanguage": "en",
"active": true,

{
"value": test@sap.com,
"type": "work",
"primary": true
}
],

"primary": true
}
```

## PUT /api/v1/scim2/Users/<UUID> Rewrites the information related to the specified by <UUID>.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters:
- id: <UUID>. You must use a user's UUID and not a user name.

- Request Body: User schema containing the information to update.
For an example user schema see the POST request in /scim2/Users. For information on role assignment, see Assigning Roles to Users and Groups. For information on additional parameter options, see Optional User Parameters.

| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/scim+json (User Schema)
| See GET for an example response. The response should include updated user information.
|




## PATCH /api/v1/scim2/Users/<UUID> Updates a user with the submitted changes. Any properties not included in the user schema will remain unchanged.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters:
- id: <UUID>. You must use a user's UUID and not a user name.

- Request Body: User schema containing the information to update. The operations that are permitted with PATCH are: add, replace, and remove.
The following example adds a role to the specified user. 

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:PatchOp"
],
"Operations": [
{
"op": "add",
"path": "roles",
"value": [
{
"value": "PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Content_Viewer",
"display": "BI_Content_Viewer",
"primary": true
}
]
}
]
}
```




For information on role assignment, see Assigning Roles to Users and Groups. For information on additional parameter options, see Optional User Parameters.

| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/scim+json (User Schema)
| See GET for an example response. The response should include updated user information.
|




## DELETE /api/v1/scim/Users/<UUID> Deletes the user specified by <UUID>.
When the user is deleted, the ownership of the user's files are transferred to the System Owner. The deleted user's public files will remain in the Public folder. Any private files will be moved to the System Owner's private folder.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters:
- id: <UUID>. You muse use a user's UUID and not a user name.

- Request Body: None

| Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 200: OK

|

# /scim2/Users/.searchSearch for and get a list of users.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## POST /api/v1/scim2/Users/.search Searches for and gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: User Schema
The following example schema searches for a list of users based on a username string:

```
{
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:SearchRequest"],
"attributes": ["displayName", "userName"],
"filter":
"displayName sw \"h\"",
"startIndex": 1,
"count": 10
}
```




The following filter options are supported in the request body: - (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, username.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the user schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

Example POST request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim2/Users/.search

| Example Response

# /scim2/GroupsAllows you to create a team or get a list of teams.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## GET /api/v1/scim2/Groups Gets a list of teams.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Optional: x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- Parameters:
- (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, username.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the group schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

- Request Body: None

Example GET request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim2/Groups?filter=displayName sw "t"&count=1
| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 403: Forbidden

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| 

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:ListResponse"
],
"totalResults": 94,
"startIndex": 1,
"itemsPerPage": 1,
"Resources": [
{

"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:core:2.0:Group"
```

## POST /api/v1/scim2/Groups Creates a team based on the information provided.

```
}
}
```

## PATCH /api/v1/scim2/Groups/<UUID> Updates the team with the submitted changes. Any properties not included in the user schema will remain unchanged.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

-
- Parameters: id: <UUID>. You must use the team's UUID and not a team name.

- Request Body: Group schema containing the information to update. The operations that are permitted with PATCH are: add, replace, and remove.
The following example adds a role to the specified team:

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:PatchOp"
],
"Operations": [
{
"op": "add",
"path": "urn:sap:params:scim:schemas:extension:sac:2.0:group-roles",
"value": {
"roles": [
{
"value": "PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Content_Creator",
"display": "BI_Content_Creator"
},
{
"value": "PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Admin",
"display": "BI_Admin"
},
{
"value": "PROFILE:sap.epm:Admin",
"display": "Admin"
}
]
}
}
]
}
```




The following example removes two users from the specified team:

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:PatchOp"
],
"Operations": [
{
"op": "remove",
"path": "members[value eq \"c8591b11-0ba2-4528-8702-83b498685a80\" or value eq \"9f286de7-864f-4c5e-a997-424124d155bc\"]"
}
]
}
```




| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/scim+json (User Schema)
| See GET for an example response. The response should include updated user information.
|

# /scim2/Groups/.searchSearch for and get a list of teams.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## POST /api/v1/scim2/Groups/.search Searches for and gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: User Schema
The following example schema searches for teams:

```
{
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:SearchRequest"],
"startIndex": 1,
"count": 1
}
```




The following filter options are supported in the request body: - (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, username.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the group schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

Example POST request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim2/Groups/.search

| Example Response

# /scim3/GroupsAllows you to create a team, or get a list of teams, or roles and its members.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## GET /api/v1/scim3/Groups Gets a list of teams or roles.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Optional: x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- Parameters:
- (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, team name.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the group schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

- Request Body: None

Example 1:
GET request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim3/Groups?filter=urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:2.0:Group:type eq "authorization”&displayName sw “Admin
| Response
| Example 1 Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 403: Forbidden

- 401: Unauthorized

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| This request returns all roles on the tenant that start with Admin.

# /scim3/Groups/<UUID>Allows you to get roles and team information, update a role or team, patch a role or team, or delete a role or team.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## GET /api/v1/scim3/Groups/<UUID> Gets information about the team or role specified by <UUID>. The ID must be set to a team's UUID or role's UUID and not a team name or role name.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Optional: x-csrf-token: <fetch>

- Parameters: id: <UUID>

- Request Body: None

Example get request using a team UUID:
GET request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim3/Groups/523d31f7-e5a5-453a-b8f0-327c6de333c8
| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 401: Unauthorized

- 200: OK

Format: application/scim+json (Group Schema)
| 

## PATCH /api/v1/scim3/Groups/<UUID> Updates the specified role or team with the submitted changes. Any properties not included in the schema will remain unchanged. The ID must be set to a role’s UUID or a team's UUID, and not a role name or team name.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- Parameters: id: <UUID>

- Request Body: Group schema containing the information to update. The operations that are permitted with PATCH are: add, replace, and remove.
The following example is a PATCH request to a role:

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:PatchOp"
],
"Operations": [
{
"op": "add",
"path": "members",
"value": [
{
"value": "4feedf5f-3d41-4f8e-8491-328507ae0f50",
"type": "User",
"display": "NICOLE DOE",
"$ref": "/api/v1/scim3/Users/4feedf5f-3d41-4f8e-8491-328507ae0f50"
}
]
},
{
"op": "replace",
"path": "urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:2.0:Group:description",
"value": "patch test"
}
]
}
```




| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 404: Not found

- 403: Forbidden

- 401: Unauthorized

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/scim+json (User Schema)
| See GET for an example response. The response should include updated user information.
|




# /scim3/Groups/.searchSearch for and get a list of roles or teams.

## Prerequisite - x-csrf-token You must get a x-csrf-token and include it in the header of every POST, PUT, PATCH or DELETE request.
For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token.

## POST /api/v1/scim3/Groups/.search Searches for and gets a list of users.
- HTTP Headers:
- Authorization: Bearer <access_token>

- x-sap-sac-custom-auth: true

- x-csrf-token: <csrf_token>

- Parameters: None

- Request Body: User Schema
The following example schema searches for teams and roles where the displayName starts with Team :

```
{
"schemas": ["urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:SearchRequest"],
"filter": "id sw \"Team\""
}
```




The following filter options are supported in the request body: - (Optional) sortBy: a user attribute to sort the results by. For example, username.

- (Optional) sortOrder: the order to used to display the results. Set to either ascending or descending. By default, an ascending sort order is used.

- (Optional) startIndex: the index of the first user to fetch. For example, if the start index is set to 10, the tenth user will be the first user returned.

- (Optional) count: the number of users to return on each page.

- (Optional) filter=<attribute>: adds a filter to the request. See the group schema for available attributes. All operators are supported.

Example POST request: <TENANT_URL>/api/v1/scim3/Groups/.search
| Response
| Example Response
|

|   - 500: Internal server error

- 403: Forbidden

- 401: Unauthorized

- 400: Bad request

- 200: OK

Format: application/json
| 

```
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:api:messages:2.0:ListResponse"
],
"totalResults": 1,
"startIndex": 1,
"itemsPerPage": 1,
"Resources": [
{
"schemas": [
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:core:2.0:Group",
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:2.0:Group"
],
"id": "989e84c9-f880-4713-a647-ae3d6fadbd36",
"meta": {
"resourceType": "Group",
"created": "2023-06-08T18:51:51.090Z",
"lastModified": "2023-12-22T19:55:18.689Z",

},
```

# Optional User ParametersYou can add optional parameters to the user schema when creating or modifying a user with the API.

## photos The photo parameter may be added directly to the user schema:  | Parameter
| Description
| Allowed Values
|

| photos
| Gets the user's user-profile photo from the link provided.
| You must provide both a value and type.
- "value": "<Photo URL">"

- "type": "photo"

|




Example:

```
"photos": [
{
"value": "https://myphotos.com/profile.png",
"type": "photo"
}
],
```




## preferredLanguage The preferredLanguage parameter may be added directly to the user schema:   | Parameter
| Description
| Allowed Values
| Default Value
|

| preferredLanguage
| The language to view SAP Analytics Cloud in.
|  - ISO 639-1 two-letter language code. For example, en.

- Concatenation of an ISO 639-1 two-letter language code, a dash, and ISO 3166-1 two-letter country code. For example, en-us.

| en
|




Example:

```
"preferredLanguage": "en",
```




## user-custom-parameters The following parameters must be included in an urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:user-custom-parameters:1.0 block within the user schema.   | Parameter
| Description
| Allowed Values
| Default Value
|

| cleanUpNotificationsNumberOfDays
| The date after which you want the system to delete notifications. Otherwise, the system keeps the most recent 500 notifications.
| 0,1,3,7, or 14
| 0
|

| dataAccessLanguage
| The default language for displaying stories created from live data connections.
|  - ISO 639-1 two-letter language code. For example, en.

- Concatenation of an ISO 639-1 two-letter language code, a dash, and ISO 3166-1 two-letter country code. For example, en-us.

| en
|

| dateFormatting
| The date display format.
|  - MMM d, yyyy

- MMM dd, yyyy

- yyyy.MM.dd

- dd.MM.yyyy

- MM.dd.yyyy

- yyyy/MM/dd

- dd/MM/yyyy

- MM/dd/yyyy

| MMM d, yyyy
|

| isConcurrent
| Set whether or not the user has a concurrent license.
| true orfalse
| false
|

| marketingEmailOptIn
| To email the user information about product updates and learning opportunities, enable this feature.
| true orfalse
| false
|

| numberFormatting
| The number format.
| 1,234.56, 1.234,56 or 1 234,56
| 1,234.56
|

| preferredLanguage
| The language to view SAP Analytics Cloud in.
|  - ISO 639-1 two-letter language code. For example, en.

- Concatenation of an ISO 639-1 two-letter language code, a dash, and ISO 3166-1 two-letter country code. For example, en-us.

| en
|

| systemNotificationsEmailOptIn
| To email the user information on system activities, for example when a new password is set, enable this feature.
| true orfalse
| true
|

| timeFormatting
| The time display format.
| H:mm:ss, h:mm:ss a or h:mm:ss A
| H:mm:ss
|




Example:

```
"urn:ietf:params:scim:schemas:extension:sap:user-custom-parameters:1.0": {
"dataAccessLanguage": "en",
"dateFormatting": "MMM d, yyyy",
"timeFormatting": "H:mm:ss",
"numberFormatting": "1,234.56",
"cleanUpNotificationsNumberOfDays": 0,
"systemNotificationsEmailOptIn": true,
"marketingEmailOptIn": false,
"isConcurrent": true
},
```




For more information, see the example response in /scim/Users.

# Assigning Roles to Users and GroupsWhen creating or modifying users and groups, you can also assign roles using the User and Team Provisioning API.
You must use the role ID when assigning roles to users and groups.
Depending on the licenses included in your subscription, some or all of the following standard application roles will be available: - PROFILE:sap.epm:Viewer

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Modeler

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Planner_Reporter

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Admin

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Content_Creator

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_Content_Viewer

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Boardroom_Viewer

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Boardroom_Creator

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Predictive_Content_Creator

- PROFILE:sap.epm:HCP_Content_Creator

- PROFILE:sap.epm:HCP_Content_Viewer

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Analytics_Hub_Admin

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Analytics_Hub_Content_Creator

- PROFILE:sap.epm:Analytics_Hub_Content_Viewer

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_RESTRICTED_CONTENT_CREATOR

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_RESTRICTED_CONTENT_VIEWER

- PROFILE:sap.epm:BI_RESTRICTED_TENANT_ADMIN

Custom roles will have IDs in the following format: PROFILE:<t.#>:<role_name> where t.# is the Content Namespace listed in  (Main Menu)   System   Administration  System Configuration.
For more information, see Standard Application Roles.

## GET /v1/audit/activities/exportActivities Returns the user activities log as a CSV file.

### URL Parameters  - (Optional) csvName: The name of the CSV file that will be generated. If left unspecified, the file will be named activities.csv
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/audit/activities/exportActivities?csvName=<FileName>.

- (Optional) pageSize: The number of entries on each page. The minimum number is 1, and the maximum is 100,000. By default, the page size is set to 100,000.
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/audit/activities/exportActivities?pageSize=100.

- (Optional) pageIndex: The page number to be retrieved based on the specified page size. The minimum page index is 1. By default, the page index is 1.
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/audit/activities/exportActivities?pageIndex=10.

- (Optional) sortKey: The column key that the log will be sorted by. This can be set to: type, fileName, description, userName, status, activity, or timestamp. By default the sort key is set totimestamp.
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/audit/activities/exportActivities?sortKey=status.

- (Optional) sortDescending: The number of entries on each page. The minimum: Sets whether the log will be sorted in descending order. Set to FALSE to sort in ascending order.
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/audit/activities/exportActivities?sortDescending=TRUE.

### Successful Response   | HTTP Status Code
| Returns
|

| 200
| Successful operation
A CSV file containing user activities will be generated.
|




- (optional) till: The end date of a range that will be used to filter the log by the sortkey or first matched timestamp.
For example, https://<TENANT_URL>/api/v1/monitoring/client?till=2024-10-28T12:09:29.879Z.

PAGE 138: /api/v1/ps
URL: https://help.sap.com/docs/SAP_ANALYTICS_CLOUD/14cac91febef464dbb1efce20e3f1613/056ba2d927864f4c81115cdbd73cadfa.html
Content length: 2693 chars
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# /api/v1/psThe Schedule Publication API allows you to create, update, and delete schedules using APIs.

## Prerequisites  - You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud tenant URL.

- You must have a SAP Analytics Cloud user.

- You must configure OAuth to work with your application. The Multi Action Service supports two OAuth authentication flows: - OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant - For information, see Configuring OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Grant Workflow in Setting up Authentication. As multi action APIs are supposed to be conducted under business user context, set Purpose to Interactive Usage when you configure the OAuth client.

- OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion - You need to have a trusted identity provider added to SAP Analytics Cloud. You can use the SAML Bearer Token issued by your identity provider to fetch the access token. For more information on how to add a trusted identity provider, see Add a Trusted Identity Provider in Set Up Third-Party Access with OAuth Clients.
The authorization code workflow generally requires the end-user to input the credentials to logon SAP Analytics Cloud explicitly to get the authorization code and continue the authentication. Since the consumption of multi action API can be embedded in a fully automated process with no user interference, the OAuth 2.0 SAML Bearer Assertion workflow could be an alternative solution.

- You must get a valid CSRF token before making any POST request. For more information, see Get a Valid CSRF Token for the Multi Action API.

## API Endpoints and Parameters    | Endpoint
| Description
|

| /schedules/template (GET)
| Allows you to request for a payload template prefilled with properties and values.
|

| /schedules (POST)
| Allows you to create single or recurrence schedule publication.
|

| /schedules/{{schedule.Id}} (PATCH)
| Allows you to update properties of your schedule.
|

| /schedules/{{schedule.Id}} (DEL)
| Allows you to delete a single or series of schedules.
|




## Limitations The following limitations apply when a schedule is published using APIs: - The schedule takes five additional minutes over current time if the recurrence type is 1 (a single occurence), runNow is false, and runOnceStartDate field is not there in payload.

- Only ISO date time is supported.

- When runNow is true and runOnce field also has valid/invalid data, runNow will be considered.

- When the number of occurrences and end date are given, the number of occurrences will be considered.

- When updating the recurrence, only firstrun parameter should be available.

- Page range is not supported.

- If the page resolution is entered wrong, schedule will be created with default resolution.

# Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST, PATCH and DEL RequestsBefore being able to send POST, PATCH, DEL HTTP requests to the service, make sure you have a valid CSRF token first.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, including the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send PATCH/POST/DEL request to the service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token
|

| Header Value
| fetch
|




## Response The CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the post/patch/del request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

## Setting Up the OAuth Client for the Translation Service To send requests to the service, you must first set up an OAuth client on the SAP Analytics Cloud system. This requires administrator access.
For any Two-Legged OAuth connection, the Translation API runs a check on the OAuth Client used to authenticate. Only a valid OAuth Client can use the API.
An OAuth Client is considered valid for the Translation API when:  - Purpose is set to API Access.

- The Translation Service is listed under Access in the list of supported APIs.

-  From the side navigation, choose  System   Administration.

-  Choose the App Integration tab.

-  Under Configure Clients, copy the Token URL. It will be needed later in this procedure.

-  Under Configured Clients, select Add a New OAuth Client.

-  In the dialog, add a Name for the OAuth client.

-  Under Purpose, select API Access.

-  Under Access, select Translation Service.

-  Click Add.
After you click Add, the application generates the OAuth Client ID and the Client Secret. Make sure to note them down, as these values will be used to send requests to the service.
After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: Access token URL, OAuth Client ID, and Client Secret.

After configuring the OAuth client, you should have access to three values: - Access token URL

- OAuth Client ID

- (Client) Secret

### Authorize API Access for OAuth Clients  If you selected API Access as the Purpose for the OAuth client, follow these steps to authorize a third party application to use the public APIs without a SAML assertion:
- Perform a POST HTTPS call to the following address:
<Token URL>?grant_type=client_credentials
<Token URL> is the Token URL listed in the OAuth Clients section of the App Integration page.

- Use basic authentication, and set the OAuth client ID as the user and the secret as the password.
This call returns an access token.

- Access the required public API endpoint with the following headers:
| Header name
| Value
| Notes
|

| Authorization
| Bearer <Token>
| <Token> is the access token returned by the previous step.
|

| x-sap-sac-custom-auth
| True
|
|

| Content-Type
| application/json
| This is only applicable to POST and PATCH requests.
|




# Get a Valid CSRF Token for POST and PATCH RequestsBefore being able to send POST or PATCH HTTP requests to the service, make sure you have a valid CSRF token first.
You can get a token by sending a GET request to <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf, including the x-csrf-token: fetch header. The csrf token is then returned in the x-csrf-token response header.
Once you get the token, you can use it to send POST or PATCH requests to the service. The x-csrf-token:<token> header must be included in the request.

## API Usage   | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/csrf
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Header Name
| x-csrf-token:<token>
|

| Header Value
| fetch
|




## Response The CSRF token is returned in the x-csrf-token response header. This token can then be included in the post/patch request in the x-csrf-token:<token> header.

# /artifacts/{id}/source/xliff (GET)Allows you to download the source XLIFF for an artifact.

## API Request Details    | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/ts/artifacts/{id}/source/xliff
|

| Request Type
| GET
|

| Request Parameters
| all → true/false
If set to true, will return XLIFF with all the strings. If not only the strings which aren't translated yet in any language would be returned.
|




## Sample Response  

# /artifacts/source/xliff (POST)Allows you to download source XLIFFs for multiple artifacts at the same time.

## API Request Details    | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/ts/artifacts/source/xliff
|

| Request Type
| POST
|

| Request Parameters
| all → true/false
If set to true, will return XLIFF with all the strings. If not only the strings which aren't translated yet in any language would be returned.
|

| Sample Request
| [ "artifactid1", "artifactid2"]
|




# /artifacts/{id}/translated (PATCH)Allows you to upload the translated XLIFFs for an artifact.

## API Request Details    | URL
| <tenant-url>/api/v1/ts/artifacts/{id}/translated
|

| Request Type
| PATCH
|

| Sample Request
| Body Type: multipart/form-data
Key Type: File
Key Name: files
Value: XLIFF files
|




## Sample Response  

```
{
"id": "5E1882E87B1A6B3B3BFF6105DCBC20A1",
"message": "Successfully uploaded XLIFF files",
"uploadedFiles": [
"Test_de.xlf"
],
"errors": [],
"CallbackDetails": {
"responseDesc": "{\"success\":true,\"error\":\"\",\"timestamps\":{\"getArtifactMetadataStrings\":273,\"updateNameAndDescTranslations\":222,\"updateResourceProperties LOAD\":133,\"updateResourceProperties SAVE\":237,\"updateAvailableTranslationsTotal\":892},\"totalElapsed\":927}",
"responseCode": 200
}
}
```
